Ruling on Maki: Only Ifrad Hajj Permitted
Ruling that Maki cannot perform Tamattu' or Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Maki regarding types of Hajj and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of Tamattu' and Qiran.

Core Idea
A Maki is restricted to Ifrad; Tamattu' and Qiran are valid but sinful.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that a person whose home is within the miqat of Makkah (a Maki) is limited to performing Ifrad Hajj. The proof is drawn from the Quranic verse restricting the concession of Tamattu' to those whose families are not present at the Masjid al-Haram. Within the Hanafi school, there is a significant disagreement on whether a Maki's performance of Tamattu' or Qiran is invalid or merely sinful, with the relied-upon view being that it is valid but deficient, requiring a compensatory sacrifice (dam jabar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
Locate the explicit statement in the main text: 'والُمكي يفرد فقط' (The Maki performs Ifrad only). This establishes the default rule.
2
Understand the definition of Maki
The commentary defines Maki as one whose home is within the miqat boundaries, citing the verse 'ذلك لمن لم يكن أهله حاضر المسجد الحرام' (That is for those whose family is not present at the Masjid al-Haram).
The miqat is the boundary for entering ihram.
3
Analyze the proof from Quran and Hadith
The verse restricts the concession of Tamattu' to non-residents. The Hadith of the Prophet shows that one with a hady cannot exit ihram, reinforcing the rule for residents.
The proof is dalil naqli with zanni dalala.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two views: Ibn al-Humam holds Tamattu'/Qiran is invalid (batil); the author of Al-Bahr holds it is valid but sinful, requiring a dam jabar. The commentary supports the second view based on the principle that dam obligation presupposes validity.
The mufta bihi is the second view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب القرآن والتمتع. (واعتمر، ولا يتحلّل منها ثم أحرم للحج كما مرّ، وحَلَق يوم النحر، وحَلّ من إحراميه. والمكي يفرد فقط). (على التقليد). (واعتمر، ولا يتحلّل منها): أي من العمرة، وهذا عند سوق الهدي، أمَّا إذا لم يَسُق الهَدْي يتحلّلُ من إحرام العمرة كما مرّ. (ثم أحرم للحج كما مرّ): أي يومُ التّروية، وقبله أفضل، وحَلَق يومَ النحر، وحل من إحراميه. (والمكي يفرد فقط): أي لا قران له، ولا تمتع. قوله: واعتمر؛ أي إذا دخل مكة طاف وسعى للعمرة. قوله: يتحلّل منها؛ أي بالحلق ونحوه، بل يبقى محرماً بقول النبي: ولولا أن مَعِي الهدي لأحللت. قوله: أفضل؛ لكونه أشقّ وأنسب بالمسارعة إلى الخير. قوله: والمكي؛ أي الذي هو من أهل مكة وكذا الذي بينهما وبين المواقيت، وهو المراد بقوله: ذَلِكَ لِمَن لَّمْ يَكُنْ أهْلُهُ حَاضِرِى الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ. قوله: فقط؛ أي ليس له إلا الإفراد بالحج وإن اعتمر قبله في أشهر الحج. قوله: أي لا قران ... الخ؛ يحتمل محملين: الأول: نفي المشروعية والوجود، فيبطل تمتعه وقرانه. الثاني: نفي الحل، بمعنى أنه يصح منه لو فعل، لكنه يأثم به، اختار ابن الهمام في «الفتح» الأول، واختار صاحب «البحر» وغيره الثاني، ويؤيده أنهم ذكروا أنه لو تمتع المكي أو قرن فعليه دم جبر لا دم شكر، ووجوب الدم متفرع على الصحة. لكن إن أتى بالقرآن أو التمتع فهو صحيح ولكنه ناقص وعليه دم جبران.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Qiran and Tamattu'. (And he performs Umrah, and does not break the ihram from it, then he enters into ihram for Hajj as before, and shaves on the Day of Nahr, and exits from both ihrams. And the Maki performs Ifrad only). (Based on taqlid). (And he performs Umrah, and does not break the ihram from it): meaning from the Umrah, and this is when he brings a hady. As for when he does not bring a hady, he breaks the ihram of Umrah as before. (Then he enters into ihram for Hajj as before): meaning on the day of Tarwiyah, and before it is better, and he shaves on the Day of Nahr, and exits from both ihrams. (And the Maki performs Ifrad only): meaning he has no Qiran and no Tamattu'. His statement: 'and he performs Umrah'; meaning that when he enters Makkah, he performs tawaf and sa'y for Umrah. His statement: 'he does not break the ihram from it'; meaning by shaving and the like, rather he remains in ihram due to the Prophet's saying: 'Were it not that I have a hady, I would have exited ihram.' His statement: 'better'; because it is more difficult and more appropriate for hastening to good. His statement: 'and the Maki'; meaning one who is from the people of Makkah and likewise one who is between them and the miqats, and he is the one intended by His statement: 'That is for those whose family is not present at the Masjid al-Haram.' His statement: 'only'; meaning he has nothing except Ifrad for Hajj, even if he performed Umrah before it in the months of Hajj. His statement: 'meaning no Qiran... etc.'; it has two interpretations: The first: negation of legality and existence, so his Tamattu' and Qiran become invalid. The second: negation of permissibility, meaning that if he does it, it is valid but he sins thereby. Ibn al-Humam chose the first in al-Fath, and the author of al-Bahr and others chose the second. It is supported by the fact that they mentioned that if a Maki performs Tamattu' or Qiran, he must offer a dam of jabar, not a dam of shukr, and the obligation of dam is based on validity. But if he performs Qiran or Tamattu', it is valid but deficient, and he must offer a dam of jabar.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling of Hajj for a resident of Makkah (Maki). The main text states that the Maki only performs Ifrad (individual Hajj) and cannot perform Tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj with a break) or Qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram). The commentary explains that the Maki is defined as one whose family resides within the boundaries of the Haram, and the Quranic verse (2:196) restricts the concession of Tamattu' to those whose families are not present. The Prophet's hadith is cited to show that one with a hady cannot exit ihram, reinforcing the rule. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Ibn al-Humam holds that if a Maki does Tamattu' or Qiran, it is invalid (batil) and he sins. The author of Al-Bahr and others hold that it is valid but sinful, requiring a dam of jabar (compensatory sacrifice) rather than a dam of shukr (thanksgiving). The author of the commentary seems to lean towards the second view, noting that the obligation of dam presupposes the validity of the acts. Therefore, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that a Maki's Tamattu' or Qiran is valid but sinful and requires a dam of jabar.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first in the months of Hajj, then Hajj in the same year with a break in between
المكي (al-maki): A person whose home is within the miqat boundaries of Makkah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person from Makkah (Maki) performs Tamattu' Hajj?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid and recommended.
C) It is valid but sinful and requires a dam of jabar.
D) It is haram and not accepted.

Key Takeaway
A Maki is restricted to Ifrad Hajj; if he performs Tamattu' or Qiran, it is valid but sinful (makruh tahrimi) and requires a compensatory dam (dam jabar).

Definition and Conditions of Tamattu' Hajj
Defines tamattu' and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tamattu' and state its three conditions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires both Hajj and Umrah in one journey without a valid return home.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi definition of tamattu' Hajj. The text from 'Umda al-Ri'aya clarifies that tamattu' is not simply performing Umrah and Hajj in the same year; it requires a single journey without returning home. This understanding is crucial because it determines when the dam (sacrificial animal) becomes wajib. We will parse the conditions and the exception for those who bring a hady.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal term and its literal meaning
Extract the definition from the text: 'al-tamattu' is seeking ease by performing both valid rites in one journey without a valid return.' Note the linguistic root: tamattu' from mut'ah (enjoyment).
2
List the three conditions for tamattu'
From the commentary: (1) both rites performed in the months of Hajj, (2) in a single journey, (3) both rites valid (sahih).
Returning home breaks the single journey.
3
Apply the condition of 'single journey' to the hady exception
If a person brings a hady during Umrah, he cannot exit ihram, so the journey continues and he remains a mutamatti'.
The hady prevents the termination of ihram.
4
Determine the consequence of spoiling a rite
If either Umrah or Hajj is invalid (fāsid), the person is not considered a mutamatti'.
Dam is only wajib for a valid tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اعتمر بلا سوق، ثم عاد إلى بلده، فقد ألم، ومع سوق تمتع. اعلم أن التمتع: هو الترفق بأداء النسكين الصحيحين في سفر واحد من غير أن يلم بأهله إلماماً صحيحاً بينهما. قوله: من اعتمر ... الخ؛ الحاصل: أن التمتع يشترط فيه أن يكون أداء الحج والعمرة كليهما في أشهر الحج في سفر واحد، فإذا اعتمر في أشهر الحج ثم رجع إلى وطنه بطل السفر السابق، فإذا حج من ذلك العام لم يكن متمتعاً؛ لعدم أدائهما في سفر واحد. هذا إذا كان لم يسق الهدي، فإن كان ساقه في إحرام العمرة يبقى متمتعاً؛ انتهاء حكم السفر السابق؛ لأنه يجب عليه العود إلى مكة؛ لعدم تحلله من الإحرام السابق بسبب الهدي. قوله: هو الترفق؛ أي طلب الرفق والسهولة والانتفاع. قوله: الصحيحين؛ قيد به لأنه لو اعتمر في أشهر الحج، وحج من عامه ذلك، وأفسد أحدهما أو كليهما لا يكون متمتعاً.
And whoever performs Umrah without a hady, then returns to his country, has 'alamma' (returned), and with a hady he is a mutamatti'. Know that tamattu' is: seeking ease by performing both valid rites in a single journey without making a valid return to his family between them. His statement: 'whoever performs Umrah...' etc.; the summary: tamattu' requires that both Hajj and Umrah be performed in the months of Hajj in a single journey. So if he performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and then returns to his homeland, the previous journey is invalidated, so if he performs Hajj that year, he is not a mutamatti' because they were not performed in a single journey. This is if he did not bring a hady. If he brought a hady in the ihram of Umrah, he remains a mutamatti' because the previous journey's ruling continues, as he must return to Makkah and cannot exit ihram due to the hady. His statement: 'it is seeking ease'; meaning seeking comfort, ease, and benefit. His statement: 'the two valid rites'; this is a qualification because if he performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj that same year, and spoiled one or both of them, he would not be a mutamatti'.
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage defines the legal term 'tamattu'' (combining Umrah and Hajj with a break) and its conditions. The author begins with a scenario: if someone performs Umrah without a sacrificial animal (hady) and then returns to his home country, he is considered to have 'alamma' (returned), and thus his tamattu' is invalidated. However, if he had a hady, he remains a mutamatti'. The definition of tamattu' is then given: performing both valid rites (Hajj and Umrah) in one journey without making a valid return to one's family between them. The commentary further clarifies that the condition of a single journey is essential; returning home after Umrah breaks the connection. The exception is when one has a hady, because with a hady he cannot exit ihram and thus the journey continues. Additionally, both rites must be valid (sahih); if either is spoiled, the person is not considered a mutamatti'. This definition highlights the key feature of tamattu': the performance of both acts in a single trip, which is what entitles one to the special concession of offering a dam instead of the separate requirements.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing both Umrah and Hajj in a single journey without returning home, with a break between them
الإلمام (al-ilmaam): Returning to one's home after Umrah, which breaks the single journey status

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person performs Umrah in the months of Hajj, returns to his home city without a hady, and then performs Hajj in the same year?
A) He is a mutamatti' and must offer a dam.
B) He is not a mutamatti' because he returned home between the two.
C) He is a mutamatti' only if he had a hady.
D) He is a mutamatti' but his Hajj is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' requires both valid rites in one journey without returning home; only then is the dam wajib.

Conditions of Tamattu': Effect of Returning Home and Bringing Sacrificial Animal
Definition and conditions of tamattu' with ilmaam and hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of tamattu' and explain how returning home and bringing a sacrificial animal affect its validity.

Core Idea
A valid tamattu' requires a single journey; returning home breaks it unless a sacrificial animal preserves the state of ihram.

This passage clarifies the definition of tamattu' in Hajj and the critical condition of a single journey. The author explains that if a pilgrim returns home after Umrah without a sacrificial animal, the tamattu' is invalidated. However, if he brings a sacrificial animal, he must remain in ihram and return for Hajj, thus preserving the tamattu'. There is also a scholarly difference on whether the definition includes a prohibition or merely describes validity.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of tamattu'
Identify the key elements: performing both Umrah and Hajj correctly, in one journey, without sound disengagement (ilmaam sahih) between them.
The definition emphasizes ease (tarafuq) and correct performance of both rites.
2
Understand the concept of ilmaam
Recognize that 'ilmaam sahih' means returning home after Umrah. This breaks the single journey and invalidates tamattu'.
The term 'alamma' (disengaged) is used to denote the breaking of the journey.
3
Analyze the effect of bringing a sacrificial animal (hady)
The presence of hady prevents full dissolution of ihram, so returning home does not break the journey; the pilgrim must return to Mecca for Hajj.
The hady acts like a chain that keeps the pilgrim bound to the original journey.
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab dispute
Ibn al-Humam interprets 'alamma' as invalidating tamattu', while al-Bahr holds it is valid but sinful; see which view is supported by the Makkan example.
The mufta bihi is that returning home without hady invalidates tamattu'.
5
Apply the timing rule for tawaf
Note that if fewer than four circuits of tawaf are performed before Shawwal, the Umrah is considered to start in the Hajj months; otherwise, tamattu' is not formed.
This expands the definition by specifying the temporal boundary of the Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اعتمر بلا سوق ، ثم عاد إلى بلده ، فقد ألم ، ومع سوق تمتع (ومن اعتمر بلا سوق ، ثم عاد إلى بلده ، فقد ألم ، ومع سوق تمتع : اعلم أن التمتع : هو التَّرفق" بأداء النسكين الصحيحين" في سفر واحد من غير أن يلم بأهله إلماماً صحيحاً (١) بينهما (٢). والثاني : نفي الحلّ، بمعنى أنه يصح منه لو فعل، لكنه يأثم به ، اختار ابن الهمام في «الفتح»(۳) الأول، واختار صاحب «البحر» (٤) وغيره الثاني، ويؤيده أنهم ذكروا أنه لو تمتع المكي أو قرن فعليه دم جبر لا دم شكر ، ووجوب الدم متفرع على الصحة. [١] قوله : من اعتمر ... الخ ؛ الحاصلُ : أنَّ التمتع يشترط فيه أن يكون أداء الحج والعمرة كليهما في أشهر الحج في سفر ،واحد ، فإذا اعتمر في أشهر الحج ثم رجع إلى وطنه بطل السفر السابق ، فإذا حج من ذلك العام لم يكن متمتعاً ؛ لعدم أدائهما في سفر واحد. لعدم هذا إذا كان لم يسق الهدي، فإن كان ساقه في إحرام العمرة يبقى متمتعاً ؛ انتهاء حكم السفر السابق ؛ لأنه يجب عليه العود إلى مكة ؛ لعدم تحلله من الإحرام السابق بسبب الهدي. [٢] قوله : هو الترفق ؛ أي طلب الرفق والسهولة والانتفاع. [٣] قوله : الصحيحين ؛ قيد به لأنه لو اعتمر في أشهر الحج، وحج من عامه ذلك، وأفسد أحدهما أو كليهما لا يكون متمتعاً. فإن طاف لها أقل من أربعة قبل أشهر الحج وأتمها فيها وحج، فقد تمتع، ولو طاف أربعة هنا لا فالذي اعتمر بلا سوق الهَدْي لَمَّا عاد إلى بلدِهِ صح المامه، فبطل تمتعه ، فقوله : فقد ألم ؛ ذَكَرَ الملزوم ، وقصد اللازم، وهو بطلان التمتع. أما إذا ساقَ الهَدْي لا يكون إلمامه صحيحاً ؛ لأنَّه لا يجوز له التحلل، فيكون عوده واجباً، فلا يكون إلمامه صحيحاً، فإذا عاد وأحرم بالحج كان متمتعاً (فإن طاف لها أقل من أربعة قبل أشهر الحج، وأتمها فيها وحج، فقد تمتع ، ولو طاف أربعة هنا لا أي لو طاف أربعة قبل أشهر الحج لا يكون متمتعاً. [١] قوله : ذكر الملزوم ؛ وهو مصدر كالقصد، أو كلاهما ماض، والضمير إلى المصنف ، حاصله أنّه أراد بقوله : فقد ألم ... ؛ بطلان تمتعه بذكر ملزومه، وهو الإلمام الصحيح. [٣] قوله : كان متمتعاً ؛ هذا إذا ترك هديه ليذبح يوم النحر، كما هو الواجب، فإن تعجل ذبحه بعد العمرة، فإن رجع إلى أهله فلا شيء عليه مطلقاً، حج من عامه ذلك أو لم يحج ، وإن لم يرجع إليهم فإن لم يحج فلا شيء عليه، وإن حج في عامه لزمه دمان: دم المتعة، ودمّ بسبب ذبحه الهدي في غير وقته. كذا في «البحر». [٤] قوله : أقل ... الخ ؛ الأصل في هذا أنّ التمتع لا يكون إلا بأداء التسكين في أشهر الحج، وهي من شوال إلى عشر ذي الحجة، فمن اعتمر في رمضان وحجَّ في ذي الحجة لا يكون متمتعاً. ومن أحرم للعمرة في رمضان ودخل مكة في آخره فطاف لها فوقع بعض طوافه في رمضان، وبعضها ليلة العيد، فإن طاف قبل شوّال أربعة أشواط أو أكثر لا يكون متمتعاً ؛ لأنّ للأكثر حكم الكل، وإن طاف قبله أقل من أربعة أشواط وأتمها في شوال يكون متمتعاً.
And whoever performs Umrah without a sacrificial animal, then returns to his city, has indeed disengaged (alamma). But with a sacrificial animal, he makes tamattu'. (And whoever performs Umrah without a sacrificial animal, then returns to his city, has indeed disengaged. And with a sacrificial animal, he makes tamattu': Know that tamattu' is seeking ease by performing both rites correctly in one journey without making a sound disengagement (ilmaam sahih) between them. The second [interpretation] is negation of dissolution, meaning that it would be valid if he did it, but he sins by doing so. Ibn al-Humam chose the first in al-Fath, and the author of al-Bahr and others chose the second, supported by the fact that they mentioned that if a Makkan performs tamattu' or qiran, he owes a compensatory dam, not a thank-offering, and the obligation of dam depends on validity. [1] His saying: 'Whoever performs Umrah...' etc.; the gist is that tamattu' requires performing both Hajj and Umrah in the months of Hajj in one journey. So if one performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and then returns to his homeland, the previous journey becomes void. If he then performs Hajj in that same year, he is not a mutamatti' because he did not perform both in one journey. ... This applies if he did not bring the sacrificial animal; if he brought it in his Umrah ihram, he remains a mutamatti' because the previous journey's ruling ends, as he must return to Mecca due to not being able to exit ihram because of the sacrificial animal. [2] His saying: 'it is seeking ease' means seeking comfort and ease and benefit. [3] His saying: 'both correct rites' is a restriction; because if he performed Umrah in the months of Hajj and performed Hajj in that same year, but spoiled one or both, he is not a mutamatti'.
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and definition from the sharh of Al-Wiqayah on the topic of tamattu' in Hajj. The author begins by stating the ruling: if a person performs Umrah without a sacrificial animal and then returns home, he has 'alamma' (disengaged), meaning his Umrah journey is considered concluded and he is no longer performing tamattu'. However, if he brings a sacrificial animal (hady) during his Umrah, then even if he returns home, he remains in the state of tamattu' because the hady prevents him from fully exiting ihram until the animal is sacrificed, so he must return to Mecca for Hajj. The commentary then defines tamattu' as performing both Umrah and Hajj in one journey without returning home in between. There is a dispute among Hanafi scholars about whether the definition includes a prohibition or just describes the ease. Ibn al-Humam prefers the first view (prohibition), while others prefer the second (valid but sinful). The consequence is that if a Makkan performs tamattu', he owes a compensatory dam, which indicates tamattu' is valid for him. The text also explains that if one performs Umrah in the months of Hajj but then goes home, the single journey condition is broken. However, if he brought a sacrificial animal, the obligation to remain in ihram keeps the journey intact. The additional case of tawaf before the months of Hajj is then discussed: if one performs less than four circuits of tawaf before Shawwal and completes it in Shawwal, he is a mutamatti'; if he performs four or more before Shawwal, the majority of tawaf occurs outside the season, so he is not a mutamatti'. The commentary concludes with details on ruling for someone who slaughters the hady early.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): The combination of Umrah and Hajj in one journey during the months of Hajj, without returning home between them, with a sacrificial animal required.
الإلمام (al-ilmaam): The act of returning home after Umrah during the Hajj season; a 'sound ilmaam' breaks the single journey and invalidates tamattu'.
الهدي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim during Umrah, which prevents full dissolution of ihram until its sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of returning home after Umrah without a sacrificial animal during the months of Hajj?
A) Tamattu' remains valid.
B) Tamattu' becomes invalid.
C) The pilgrim must repeat both Umrah and Hajj.
D) The pilgrim must sacrifice an additional animal.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' requires a continuous journey; returning home breaks it unless a sacrificial animal preserves the state of ihram.

Determining Tamattu' by Tawaf Circuits and Ilmaam
Ruling on when Tamattu' is established based on tawaf circuits and ilmaam conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that establish Tamattu' in Hajj, specifically regarding the number of tawaf circuits before Shawwal and the effect of ilmaam with or without a sacrificial animal.

Core Idea
Tamattu' is established only if less than four tawaf circuits are performed before Shawwal, and ilmaam (return home) after Umrah invalidates it unless a sacrificial animal is brought.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya clarifies the precise conditions under which a pilgrim becomes a Mutamatti'. The key revolves around the timing of tawaf circuits relative to the Hajj months and the status of ilmaam. Understanding these rules prevents common errors in determining the obligation of the sacrificial animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Umrah followed by Hajj in the same journey. The ruling is whether this combination constitutes Tamattu', which requires a sacrificial animal (dam). The passage explains when it is and is not Tamattu'.
2
Apply the circuit rule
The month in which the tawaf is considered to occur is determined by the majority of circuits. If four or more circuits are performed before Shawwal, the tawaf is attributed to Ramadan, so the Umrah is not in the Hajj months, and Tamattu' is not established. If less than four are done before Shawwal and the remainder in Shawwal, then the Umrah is in the Hajj months, and Tamattu' is established.
The principle 'al-akthar yanzilu manzilat al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) is applied.
3
Understand the ilmaam condition
Ilmaam refers to completing Umrah with valid tahallul (exit from ihram) and returning to one's home country. If a person performs Umrah without bringing a sacrificial animal and returns home, his ilmaam is valid, and this invalidates Tamattu'. If he brought a sacrificial animal, he cannot exit ihram (ilmaam invalid), so he remains a Mutamatti' and must return for Hajj.
Bringing the sacrificial animal makes the person a Qarin (remaining in ihram for both), but if he returns and then does Hajj, it is considered Tamattu' with a valid ilmaam? Actually the text says he is a Mutamatti'.
4
Handle early slaughter of the sacrificial animal
If the Mutamatti' slaughters his sacrificial animal after Umrah (before the Day of Sacrifice), the ruling depends on whether he returns to his family. If he returns, nothing is required; if he does not return and then performs Hajj that year, he owes two dams: one for Tamattu' and one for slaughtering out of time.
This is a special case detailed in the commentary, illustrating the consequences of violating the time of sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فإن طاف لها أقل من أربعة قبل أشهر الحج وأتمها فيها وحج، فقد تمتع، ولو طاف أربعة هنا لا فالذي اعتمر بلا سوق الهَدْي لَمَّا عاد إلى بلدِهِ صح المامه، فبطل تمتعه ،
[1]
فقوله : فقد ألم؛ ذَكَرَ الملزوم، وقصد اللازم، وهو بطلان التمتع. أما إذا ساقَ الهَدْي لا يكون إلمامه صحيحاً ؛ لأنَّه لا يجوز له التحلل، فيكون عوده واجباً، فلا يكون إلمامه صحيحاً، فإذا عاد وأحرم بالحج كان متمتعاً
(فإن طاف لها أقل من أربعة قبل أشهر الحج، وأتمها فيها وحج، فقد تمتع ، ولو طاف أربعة هنا لا أي لو طاف أربعة قبل أشهر الحج لا يكون متمتعاً. [١] قوله : ذكر الملزوم ؛ وهو مصدر كالقصد، أو كلاهما ماض، والضمير إلى المصنف ، حاصله أنّه أراد بقوله : فقد ألم ... ؛ بطلان تمتعه بذكر ملزومه، وهو الإلمام الصحيح. (٢) قوله : التحلل ؛ أي الخروج من إحرام العمرة بالحلق ونحوه.
[٣] قوله : كان متمتعاً ؛ هذا إذا ترك هديه ليذبح يوم النحر، كما هو الواجب، فإن تعجل ذبحه بعد العمرة، فإن رجع إلى أهله فلا شيء عليه مطلقاً، حج من عامه ذلك أو لم يحج ، وإن لم يرجع إليهم فإن لم يحج فلا شيء عليه، وإن حج في عامه لزمه دمان: دم المتعة، ودمّ بسبب ذبحه الهدي في غير وقته. كذا في «البحر». [٤] قوله : أقل ... الخ ؛ الأصل في هذا أنّ التمتع لا يكون إلا بأداء التسكين في أشهر الحج، وهي من شوال إلى عشر ذي الحجة، فمن اعتمر في رمضان وحجَّ في ذي الحجة لا يكون متمتعاً.
ومن أحرم للعمرة في رمضان ودخل مكة في آخره فطاف لها فوقع بعض طوافه في رمضان، وبعضها ليلة العيد، فإن طاف قبل شوّال أربعة أشواط أو أكثر لا يكون متمتعاً ؛ لأنّ للأكثر حكم الكل، وإن طاف قبله أقل من أربعة أشواط وأتمها في شوال يكون متمتعاً.
Book of Hajj: Chapter of Qiran and Tamattu'. If he performs less than four [circuits] of tawaf for it [the Umrah] before the months of Hajj, and completes them in them and performs Hajj, then he has performed Tamattu'. And if he performs four circuits here, no. So, the one who performs Umrah without bringing the sacrificial animal, when he returned to his country, his ilmaam is valid, so his Tamattu' is invalid. [1] His saying: 'so he has performed ilmaam'; he mentioned the necessary condition, and intended the necessary consequence, which is the invalidity of Tamattu'. As for when he brings the sacrificial animal, his ilmaam is not valid; because it is not permissible for him to exit ihram, so his return is obligatory, so his ilmaam is not valid. So if he returns and assumes ihram for Hajj, he is a Mutamatti'. (If he performs less than four before the months of Hajj, and completes them in them and performs Hajj, then he has performed Tamattu'. And if he performs four here, no; i.e., if he performs four circuits before the months of Hajj, he is not a Mutamatti'. [1] His saying: he mentioned the necessary condition; it is a verbal noun like intent, or both are past tense, and the pronoun refers to the author. The gist is that by his saying 'so he has performed ilmaam' he meant the invalidity of his Tamattu' by mentioning its necessary condition, which is valid ilmaam. (2) His saying: 'al-tahallul'; i.e., exiting from the ihram of Umrah by shaving and the like. [3] His saying: 'he is a Mutamatti''; this is if he leaves his sacrificial animal to be slaughtered on the Day of Sacrifice, as is obligatory. But if he hastens to slaughter it after Umrah, then if he returns to his family, there is nothing upon him at all, whether he performs Hajj that year or not. And if he does not return to them, then if he does not perform Hajj, there is nothing upon him; if he performs Hajj that year, two sacrificial animals are obligatory upon him: the sacrificial animal of Tamattu' and a sacrificial animal due to slaughtering the sacrificial animal out of its time. Thus in al-Bahr. [4] His saying: 'less' etc.; the principle in this is that Tamattu' only occurs by performing the settling in the months of Hajj, which are from Shawwal to the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah. So whoever performs Umrah in Ramadan and performs Hajj in Dhu al-Hijjah is not a Mutamatti'. And whoever assumes ihram for Umrah in Ramadan and enters Makkah at its end, then performs tawaf for it, and some of his tawaf occurs in Ramadan and some on the night of Eid, then if he performs four circuits or more before Shawwal, he is not a Mutamatti'; because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And if he performs less than four circuits before it and completes them in Shawwal, he is a Mutamatti'.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya explains the ruling on determining when a person performing Umrah becomes a Mutamatti' for Hajj. The core ruling is that the number of tawaf circuits performed before the start of Shawwal (the first month of Hajj) determines whether the person is considered to have performed Tamattu'. If he performs less than four circuits before Shawwal and completes the remaining circuits in Shawwal, then continues with Hajj, he is a Mutamatti'. If he performs four or more circuits before Shawwal, he is not a Mutamatti'. This is because the majority of the tawaf determines the month it is considered to have been performed in. The commentary then discusses the issue of 'ilmaam', which refers to the completion of Umrah with a valid exit from ihram. If a person performs Umrah without bringing a sacrificial animal and then returns to his home country, his ilmaam is valid, and his Tamattu' is invalidated. If he brings a sacrificial animal, his ilmaam is not valid because he cannot exit ihram, so he must return and perform Hajj, making him a Mutamatti'. The commentary also addresses the case of someone who slaughters his sacrificial animal early (after Umrah instead of on the Day of Sacrifice). If he returns to his family, nothing is required. If he does not return and then performs Hajj that year, he owes two sacrificial animals: one for Tamattu' and one for slaughtering out of time. Finally, the passage confirms that Tamattu' only occurs if the Umrah is performed within the months of Hajj (Shawwal to Dhu al-Hijjah). An example is given: if someone performs Umrah in Ramadan and some of the tawaf occurs in Ramadan, the number of circuits before Shawwal determines the ruling.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first in the months of Hajj, then exits ihram, and later enters ihram for Hajj from Makkah, with a sacrificial animal required.
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
إلمام (ilmaam): Completion of Umrah with a valid exit from ihram (tahallul) and returning to one's home country.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim performs 3 tawaf circuits for Umrah on the last day of Ramadan and the remaining 4 circuits on the 1st of Shawwal, then performs Hajj, are they a Mutamatti' according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because they completed the tawaf in Shawwal.
B) No, because the majority of circuits (4) were in Shawwal? Actually 4 in Shawwal, 3 in Ramadan, so majority in Shawwal, so Umrah is in Hajj months, so Yes.
C) Yes, because less than 4 circuits were performed before Shawwal.
D) No, because they performed circuits in both months.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is established only if less than four tawaf circuits are performed before the Hajj months and if the pilgrim has not performed valid ilmaam (return home) without a sacrificial animal.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tamattu' for an Afaaqi Who Goes to Another Town
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether an Afaaqi who completes Umrah in Hajj months then goes to Basra is Mutamatti'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an Afaaqi who goes to a non-hometown town after Umrah and then performs Hajj qualifies as a Mutamatti', and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
An Afaaqi who does not return to his hometown after Umrah remains in a single journey, making him a Mutamatti' according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines a nuanced ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school regarding the definition of Tamattu'. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explores whether an Afaaqi who completes Umrah, then travels to a town like Basra (not his hometown), and later performs Hajj the same year, qualifies as a Mutamatti'. The disagreement hinges on whether the 'first journey' is considered ongoing or interrupted, and whether both rituals are performed from the miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage discusses a Kufi (Afaaqi) who performs Umrah in the Hajj months, then resides in Makkah or goes to Basra (a non-hometown town), and then performs Hajj. Understand the base ruling: if he stays in Makkah, it is Tamattu' by consensus.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) on the Basra scenario
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the person is Mutamatti' because his first journey from Kufa to Makkah is considered ongoing as long as he does not return to Kufa. Going to Basra does not end the journey.
The journey is defined by the connection to the hometown.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that he is not Mutamatti' because a Mutamatti' has an 'Umrah from the miqat and a Hajj from Makkah. Here, both rituals are from the miqat (the 'Umrah from the miqat of Kufa and the Hajj from the miqat of Basra).
They define Tamattu' by the location of each ritual's start.
4
Analyze the underlying principle
The ikhtilaf centers on the definition of 'performing both rituals in one journey'. Abu Hanifa sees the journey as a continuous physical trip until the hometown is revisited. The Sahibayn consider the legal status of the miqat as the determinant.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the tarjih
The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, the person owes a dam (sacrificial animal) for Tamattu'; according to the Sahibayn, no dam is required. The text cites al-Hidayah and al-Binaya but does not explicitly choose one position.
In later Hanafi practice, the view of Abu Hanifa is often relied upon for fatwa, but the ikhtilaf remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كوفي حل من عمرته فيها، وسكن بمكة، أو بصرة، وحج فهو متمتع، ولو أفسدها، ورجع من البصرة، وقضاها وحج لا
[٢]
(۱۸) حلّ من عمرته فيها : أي في أشهر الحج، وسكن بمكة، أو بصرة، وحج فهو متمتع ) ؛ لأنَّ السَّفَرَ الأَوَّلَ لم ينته برجوعه إلى البصرة، فصار كأنه لم يخرج من الميقات. (ولو أفسدها"، ورجع من البصرة، وقضاها وحج لا)
[١]قوله : كوفي؛ أي من وطنه بكوفة، وهذا بطريق المثال ، والمراد كل من كان آفاقياً، وأما المكي فلا تمتع له. [٢] قوله : حلّ من عمرته ؛ يعني أنّ الكوفي إذا دخل مكة بإحرام العمرة فأتم وتحلل من إحرامه في أشهر الحج، ثمّ سكن بمكة إلى أيام الحج أو فيما في حكمها تما هو داخل المواقيت ، أو ذهب من مكة إلى البصرة وغيرها من البلاد، وغير وطنه فسكن فيها، ثم حج من عامه ذلك، يكون متمتعاً، وهذا في صورة السكونة بمكة اتفاقي اتفاقاً ؛ لعدم وجود ما يبطل التمتع.
وفي صورة ذهابه إلى بلدة أخرى غير وطنه اختلف فيها :
فقيل : إنه لا يكون متمتعاً بالاتفاق.
وقيل : يكون متمتعاً عنده لا عندهما. لهما : أنّ المتمتع من تكون عمرته ميقاتية وحجه مكيّاً، وهذا نسكاه ميقاتيان.
وله : أن السفر الأول قائم ما لم يعد إلى وطنه، فوجد أداء النسكين في سفر واحد. كذا في «الهداية»(۲) و«البناية»(۳).
[٣]قوله : ولو أفسدها ... الخ ؛ يعني أنّ الكوفي إذا أحرم للعمرة في أشهر الحج فأفسدها بارتكاب ما يفسدها كالجماع قبل تمام ،أفعالها ، ثم ذهب إلى البصرة وأقام فيها ثم رجع منها إلى مكة وأحرم بالعمرة من الميقات قضاء لما أفسده، وحج من عامه ذلك
A Kufi who completed his Umrah in them [the months of Hajj], and resided in Makkah or Basra, and performed Hajj, then he is a Mutamatti'. And if he spoiled it, and returned from Basra, and made it up, and performed Hajj, he is not. [2] (18) He completed his Umrah in them: i.e., in the months of Hajj, and resided in Makkah or Basra, and performed Hajj, then he is a Mutamatti'; because the first journey did not end with his return to Basra, so it is as if he did not leave the miqat. (And if he spoiled it, and returned from Basra, and made it up, and performed Hajj, he is not.) [1] His saying: 'Kufi'; i.e., one whose hometown is Kufa, and this is by way of example, and the intent is everyone who is an Afaaqi. As for the Makki, there is no Tamattu' for him. [2] His saying: 'he completed his Umrah'; meaning that the Kufi, when he enters Makkah with the ihram of Umrah and completes it and exits from his ihram in the months of Hajj, then resides in Makkah until the days of Hajj or in what is considered as such as long as he is within the miqat, or he goes from Makkah to Basra and other towns not his hometown and resides there, then performs Hajj that same year, he is a Mutamatti'. And this in the case of residing in Makkah is agreed upon unanimously; because there is nothing that invalidates the Tamattu'. And in the case of his going to another town besides his hometown, there is a difference of opinion [among the Hanafi imams]: Some say he is not a Mutamatti' by consensus. And some say he is a Mutamatti' according to him [Abu Hanifa] and not according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. For them: the Mutamatti' is one whose Umrah is from the miqat and whose Hajj is Makkan, and these two rituals are both from the miqat. And for him: the first journey remains as long as he does not return to his hometown, so the performance of the two rituals in one journey is found. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Binaya. [3] His saying: 'And if he spoiled it' etc.; meaning that the Kufi, when he assumes ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj and spoils it by committing something that spoils it, like intercourse before completing its actions, then goes to Basra and stays there, then returns from it to Makkah and assumes ihram for Umrah from the miqat to make up for what he spoiled, and performs Hajj that same year.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage from the commentary addresses the conditions under which an Afaaqi (a person whose hometown is outside the miqat) becomes a Mutamatti'. The example given is a person from Kufa. The ruling states that if such a person completes his Umrah in the months of Hajj, then either resides in Makkah or goes to another town (like Basra) that is not his hometown, and then performs Hajj in the same year, he is a Mutamatti'. This is because his first journey (from his hometown to Makkah) is considered ongoing as long as he does not return to his hometown. The commentary notes that the case of staying in Makkah is agreed upon. However, when he goes to another town (like Basra), there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he is still a Mutamatti' because the first journey continues. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), he is not a Mutamatti', because both his Umrah and Hajj are performed from the miqat (his Umrah from the miqat of Kufa and his Hajj from the miqat of Basra), and the Mutamatti' should have his Umrah from the miqat and his Hajj from Makkah. The passage then discusses a different case: if the Kufi spoils his Umrah (by having intercourse before completing it), then returns to Basra (his hometown), and then goes back to Makkah and performs a make-up Umrah from the miqat, and then performs Hajj the same year, he is not a Mutamatti'. This is because his first journey ended when he returned to his hometown after the spoilage.

Key Terms
كوفي (kūfī): A person from Kufa; used as an example for any Afaaqi (one whose hometown is outside the miqat).
آفاقي (āfāqī): A person whose hometown is outside the miqat (the designated boundaries for Hajj).
إفساد (ifsād): Spoiling the Umrah by committing prohibited acts (like intercourse) before completing its actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why is an Afaaqi who goes to Basra after Umrah and then performs Hajj not considered a Mutamatti'?
A) Because he returned to his hometown.
B) Because both his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat.
C) Because he did not perform Umrah in the Hajj months.
D) Because he brought a sacrificial animal.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa considers the journey ongoing as long as one does not return to one's hometown, while the Sahibayn focus on the miqat origin of each ritual.

The Afaqi's Tamattu' After Traveling to Another City: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explaining the tamattu' ruling and the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the tamattu' of an Afaqi who travels to a non-homeland city after Umrah, and explain the legal reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
The continuity of the journey determines tamattu': as long as you haven't returned to your homeland, the single journey persists.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement about tamattu'. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, agree that an Afaqi who performs Umrah in the Hajj months and then stays in Makkah until Hajj is a mutamatti'. However, they differ when the person travels to another city (not his original homeland) before Hajj. Understanding their reasoning reveals a fundamental principle about the definition of a 'single journey' for tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed case
State the scenario where all scholars agree the person is mutamatti': staying in Makkah after Umrah.
There is consensus when the person stays in Makkah.
2
Identify the disputed scenario
The Afaqi travels to another non-homeland city (e.g., Basra) after Umrah but before Hajj.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
He is mutamatti' because the first journey is still ongoing; no return to original homeland.
Dalil: 'The first journey remains as long as he has not returned to his homeland.'
4
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
He is not mutamatti' because both rituals are miqati; Hajj is no longer Makki.
Their dalil: 'The mutamatti' is one whose Umrah is miqati and Hajj is Makki.'
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If mutamatti', must offer dam; if not, no dam for tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : كوفي؛ أي من وطنه بكوفة، وهذا بطريق المثال ، والمراد كل من كان آفاقياً، وأما المكي فلا تمتع له. [٢] قوله : حلّ من عمرته ؛ يعني أنّ الكوفي إذا دخل مكة بإحرام العمرة فأتم وتحلل من إحرامه في أشهر الحج، ثمّ سكن بمكة إلى أيام الحج أو فيما في حكمها مما هو داخل المواقيت ، أو ذهب من مكة إلى البصرة وغيرها من البلاد، وغير وطنه فسكن فيها، ثم حج من عامه ذلك، يكون متمتعاً، وهذا في صورة السكونة بمكة اتفاقي اتفاقاً ؛ لعدم وجود ما يبطل التمتع. وفي صورة ذهابه إلى بلدة أخرى غير وطنه اختلف فيها : فقيل : إنه لا يكون متمتعاً بالاتفاق. وقيل : يكون متمتعاً عنده لا عندهما. لهما : أنّ المتمتع من تكون عمرته ميقاتية وحجه مكيّاً، وهذا نسكاه ميقاتيان. وله : أن السفر الأول قائم ما لم يعد إلى وطنه، فوجد أداء النسكين في سفر واحد. كذا في «الهداية»(٢) و«البناية»(٣). (١) كوفي : المراد به الآفاقي الذي شرع له التمتع والقرآن وكما أن البصرة مكان لأهل التمتع والقران سواء كان مكانه البصرة أو غيرها. ينظر : ((مجمع الأنهر» (١ : ٢٩١). (٢) ((الهداية (٣ : ١٩ - ٢٠). (٣) (البناية (٣: ٦٥٥ - ٦٥٦).
He said: 'Kufi' means one whose homeland is Kufa, and this is by way of example, and the intent is every Afaqi. As for the Makki, there is no tamattu' for him. [2] He said: 'He completed his Umrah' means that the Kufi, if he entered Makkah with the ihram of Umrah, completed it and exited from his ihram in the months of Hajj, then stayed in Makkah until the days of Hajj or what is in its ruling from what is within the miqat, or went from Makkah to Basra and other lands, not his homeland, and resided there, then performed Hajj that same year, he is mutamatti'. This, in the case of staying in Makkah, is agreed upon unanimously due to the absence of anything that nullifies tamattu'. In the case of his going to another town not his homeland, there is disagreement: it is said that he is not mutamatti' by agreement. And it is said that he is mutamatti' according to him (Abu Hanifa) but not according to them (the two disciples). For them (the Sahibayn): The mutamatti' is one whose Umrah is from the miqat and his Hajj is Makki, and both of these rituals are from miqat. For him (Abu Hanifa): The first journey remains as long as he has not returned to his homeland, so he has performed both rituals in one journey. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of tamattu' for an Afaqi (a person whose original homeland is outside Makkah) who performs Umrah in the months of Hajj, then either stays in Makkah or travels to another city (not his original homeland) before performing Hajj in the same year. The text begins by clarifying that 'Kufi' is an example for any Afaqi, and that a Makki (resident of Makkah) cannot perform tamattu' because tamattu' requires the Hajj to be 'Makki' (i.e., the person performs Hajj while residing in Makkah) while the Umrah is 'miqati' (performed from the miqat). It then states that if the person stays in Makkah after Umrah, all scholars agree he is mutamatti' because there is no factor to break tamattu'. However, if he travels to another city (like Basra) that is not his original homeland, there is disagreement: According to Abu Hanifa, he remains mutamatti' because his first journey from his homeland to Makkah is considered ongoing as long as he has not returned to his original homeland (watan). Therefore, performing both Umrah and Hajj in this state means they are done in one journey, which is the essence of tamattu'. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), he is not mutamatti' because his Umrah was from the miqat (since he re-entered the miqat from Basra) and his Hajj will also be from the miqat (since he is now coming from outside Makkah), so both rituals are miqati, not a combination of a miqati Umrah and a Makki Hajj. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the reference to al-Hidayah and al-Binayah.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person performing Hajj al-Tamattu', i.e., performing Umrah first in the months of Hajj, then exiting ihram, then performing Hajj in the same year.
آفاقي (afaqi): A person whose original homeland (watan asli) is outside the miqat boundaries of Makkah, i.e., not a resident of Makkah.
ميقات (miqat): The designated boundary from which one must assume ihram for Hajj or Umrah. For an Afaqi, the miqat is the specific station for his region.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what condition must be met for an Afaqi to no longer be considered mutamatti' after performing Umrah in the Hajj months?
A) He must leave Makkah to any other city
B) He must return to his original homeland (watan asli)
C) He must stay in Makkah until the day of Arafah
D) He must perform a second Umrah

Key Takeaway
An Afaqi remains mutamatti' after traveling to a non-homeland city as long as he does not return to his original homeland, per Abu Hanifa.

Effect of Travel after Spoiling 'Umrah on Tamattu' Status and Ruling on Completing a Spoiled Ritual
Explaining ruling on spoiling Umrah and effect on tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling to determine whether a person who spoils his 'Umrah during Hajj months becomes a mutamatti' when he returns to perform make-up 'Umrah and Hajj, and state the ruling on dam when a mutamatti' spoils a ritual.

Core Idea
Returning to one's homeland after spoiling 'Umrah breaks the original journey and allows tamattu'; going to a non-homeland does not.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Al-Wiqayah, clarifies a specific case: a Kufi who spoils his 'Umrah during the Hajj months, then travels to Basra (a city that is not his homeland) and later returns to Makkah to perform a make-up 'Umrah and Hajj. The text explains that he does not become a mutamatti' because his original journey is considered ongoing. However, if he first returns to Kufa (his homeland), then he becomes a mutamatti'. The passage also covers the rule when a mutamatti' spoils either the 'Umrah or the Hajj: he must complete the spoiled ritual and does not owe the dam al-tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish the case where the pilgrim goes to Basra (non-homeland) vs. returns to Kufa (homeland) after spoiling the 'Umrah.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The ruling is based on istihsan: the first journey is considered to persist until the pilgrim returns to his original homeland (watan asli). If he goes elsewhere, the journey is not broken, so he is treated as a resident of Makkah (Makki) and cannot perform tamattu'.
This is a key principle of Hanafi fiqh regarding continuity of travel.
3
Apply the exception
If he does return to his homeland (al-ilmam bi-ahlihi), the first journey is negated, and the subsequent 'Umrah and Hajj form a new journey, making him a mutamatti'.
The exception is explicitly stated: 'إلا إذا ألم بأهله'.
4
Note the rule for spoiling a ritual
If a mutamatti' spoils either the 'Umrah or the Hajj, he must complete it (go through its actions) and does not owe dam al-tamattu' because he did not perform both rituals correctly.
This is covered by the phrase: 'وأي أفسد أتمه بلا دم'.
5
Distinguish the dam
The dam for tamattu' is separate from any dam due for spoiling; in this case, the tamattu' dam is dropped, but a dam for the spoilage may be required (though not detailed in this passage).

Source Text

قوله : ولو أفسدها ... الخ ؛ يعني أنّ الكوفي إذا أحرم للعمرة في أشهر الحج فأفسدها بارتكاب ما يفسدها كالجماع قبل تمام أفعالها ، ثم ذهب إلى البصرة وأقام فيها ثم رجع منها إلى مكة وأحرم بالعمرة من الميقات قضاء لما أفسده، وحج من عامه ذلك لا يصير متمتعاً ؛ لأنّ حكم السفرِ الأَوَّلِ لَمَّا بقي بالرُّجوع إلى البصرة، فصار كأنه لم يخرج من مكة، ولا تمتع للساكن بمكة. إلا إذا ألم بأهلِه ، ثُمَّ أتى بهما ؛ لأنَّه لَمَّا أَلمَّ بِأَهِلِهِ، ثُمَّ رجع وأتى بالعمرة والحج كان هذا إنشاء سفر ؛ لإنتفاء السفرِ الأَوَّلِ بالإلمام، فاجتمع نسكان في سفر واحد فيكون متمتعاً. ( وأي أفسد أتمه بلا دم) : أي من اعتمر في أشهر الحج، وحج من عامه ، فأيهما أفسد مضى فيه ؛ لأنَّه لا يمكنه الخروج من عهدة الإحرام إلا بالأفعال، وسقط دم التمتع ؛ لأنَّه لم يترفّق بأداء النسكين الصحيحين في سفر واحد. لا يصير متمتعاً؛ لأنّ سفره السابق انتهى بالفاسدة، وصارت عمرته الصحيحة مكية، ولا تمتع لأهل مكة. [٣] قوله : مضى؛ أي يجب عليه المضي فيه وإتمامه. نعم
He said: 'And if he spoils it... etc.' means: The Kufi, if he enters ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj and spoils it by committing what spoils it, like intercourse before completing its actions, then goes to Basra and stays there, then returns from it to Makkah and assumes ihram for Umrah from the miqat to make up for what he spoiled, and performs Hajj that same year, he does not become mutamatti'; because the ruling of the first journey remained by returning to Basra, so it is as if he did not leave Makkah, and there is no tamattu' for one residing in Makkah. Except if he arrives at his family (homeland), then comes with both; because when he arrived at his family, then returned and came with the Umrah and Hajj, this is the beginning of a journey; because the first journey is negated by arriving at his family, so two rituals are combined in one journey and he becomes mutamatti'. ('And whichever he spoils, he completes it without blood') meaning: Whoever performs Umrah in the months of Hajj and performs Hajj that same year, then whichever of them he spoils, he goes on with it; because he cannot exit from the obligation of ihram except by the actions, and the blood of tamattu' is waived; because he did not enjoy the performance of both correct rituals in one journey. He does not become mutamatti'; because his previous journey ended with the spoiled one, and his correct Umrah became Makki, and there is no tamattu' for the people of Makkah. [1] He said: 'Except if he arrives... etc.' means: In this scenario, if he goes to Kufa and stays there, then travels from it to Makkah and assumes ihram for Umrah from the miqat to make up for what he previously spoiled in the months of Hajj, and performs Hajj that year, he becomes mutamatti'; because the ruling of the first journey has ended by returning to his homeland, so he is no longer Makki; when he returned and combined them in this journey, he becomes mutamatti' with this correct Umrah. [2] He said: 'And whichever' (with fatha on the hamza and shadda on the ya) means: If the mutamatti' in the months of Hajj of that year spoils his Umrah or his Hajj, one of them or both, by committing what spoils it, as will be explained in detail if Allah wills, he must complete that which he spoiled by going through its actions and then performing tahlul, and there is no blood (i.e., dam al-tamattu') upon him at that time; because he combined two correct rituals, and blood is required for spoiling, as a compensation or deterrent. [3] He said: 'He goes on' means: He must proceed with it and complete it. Yes.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on a person who spoils his Umrah (e.g., by intercourse before completing its actions) during the months of Hajj, then travels to Basra (a city other than his homeland), and later returns from Basra to Makkah to perform a make-up Umrah from the miqat, followed by Hajj in the same year. The text states that such a person is not considered mutamatti' because the first journey (from his homeland to Makkah) is considered to have ended when he returned to Basra? The reasoning given is that since the ruling of the first journey remained by returning to Basra, it is as if he never left Makkah, and thus he is like a resident of Makkah (Makki), for whom tamattu' is not valid. However, there is an exception: if he returns to his original homeland (e.g., Kufa) first, then comes back to perform Umrah and Hajj, he becomes mutamatti' because the journey is a new one, and the two rituals are combined in one journey. The text also discusses the case where a mutamatti' spoils either the Umrah or the Hajj: he must complete the spoiled ritual (mada fihi) because he cannot exit ihram without completing its actions. In this case, he does not owe the dam for tamattu' because he did not perform both rituals correctly in one journey; instead, he may owe a dam for the spoilage itself. The relied-upon ruling is that the person who spoils Umrah and then goes to Basra does not become mutamatti', but if he returns to his homeland and then comes back, he does. This is consistent with the principle that the continuity of the first journey is broken only by returning to the watan asli.

Key Terms
أفسد (afsada): To spoil the state of ihram by committing a prohibited act that nullifies the ongoing ritual (e.g., intercourse before completing Umrah).
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): The sacrificial blood (usually a sheep or goat) required from a mutamatti' for the privilege of combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey.
الإلمام بأهله (al-ilmam bi-ahlihi): Visiting or returning to one's original family and homeland (watan asli).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Kufi performs 'Umrah during Hajj months and spoils it. He then travels to Basra and stays there, then returns to Makkah to make up the 'Umrah and perform Hajj. According to the text, what is his status?
A) He is mutamatti' and must offer dam al-tamattu'.
B) He is not mutamatti' because his journey is considered continuous.
C) He is mutamatti' only if he first returns to Kufa.
D) He is considered a Makki and must perform Hajj ifrad.

Key Takeaway
A pilgrim who spoils his 'Umrah during Hajj months becomes mutamatti' only if he returns to his original homeland before returning to Makkah to perform make-up 'Umrah and Hajj; otherwise, he is not mutamatti' and owes no dam al-tamattu'.

Rulings on Perfume, Henna, and Oil for a Muhrim
Commentary on the chapter of offences for a muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalty for a muhrim who applies perfume, henna, or oil to a limb and distinguish when a dam versus sadaqah is required.

Core Idea
A muhrim who perfumes a full limb owes a dam; less requires sadaqah — henna is also perfume.

In this passage, the commentator explains the rulings for a muhrim who applies perfume, henna, or oil. The key principle is that a complete limb perfumed incurs a dam (blood sacrifice), while less than a full limb incurs sadaqah. The passage also clarifies why henna is mentioned separately despite being a type of perfume, due to scholarly disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (applying perfume, henna, or oil while in ihram) and the overall ruling: it is prohibited (haram) and carries a compensatory penalty.
2
Determine the threshold for a dam
Understand that 'a limb' means a complete limb (e.g., head, thigh). If the entire limb is perfumed, a dam is required.
Al-Kirmani's statement: if all limbs are perfumed, only one dam.
3
Understand penalty for partial perfume
If less than a full limb is perfumed, the penalty is sadaqah. If separate parts collectively equal a full limb, then a dam.
Separate applications can be summed.
4
Consider the special case of henna
Henna is singled out because of scholarly disagreement. The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith, treats henna as a perfume.
Hadith: 'Henna is a perfume' (weak chain).
5
Apply to a perfumed garment
For a garment that is mostly perfumed, a dam is only due if the muhrim wears it continuously for a day.
Source: al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنايات
إن طيب محرم عضواً، أو خَضَبَ رأسَه بِحِنَّاء، أو ادهَن بزيت
قوله : باب الجنايات ؛ لَمَّا ذكر أقسام المحرمين وأحكامهم، شرع في بيان ما يعرض لهم باعتبار الإحرام أو الحرم من الجنايات، وهو جمع جناية - بالكسر - وهو في الأصل مصدر جنى، إذا ارتكب معصية، وشاع استعماله في نفس ذلك الفعل، وهو المراد هاهنا ، ولذا أورده بلفظ : الجمع.
قوله : إن تطيب محرم ؛ الأولى طيب محرم ، كما في أكثر نسخ «الهداية»، فإنّ التطيّب لازم، فلا يمكن جعل قوله عضواً مفعولاً، ويمكن أن يقال: إنه تمييز من نسبة التطيب إلى المحرم ، والمراد بالطيب : كلّ ما له رائحة طيبة : كالبنفسج والريحان والياسمين والورود وغير ذلك.

Chapter of Offences. If a muhrim applies perfume to a limb, or dyes his head with henna, or applies oil... His saying: Chapter of Offences; when he mentioned the types of muhrim and their rulings, he began to explain what occurs to them regarding the ihram or the sanctuary of offences. It is the plural of jinaaya - with kasra - and it is originally a verbal noun of janaa, when he commits a sin, and its usage became widespread for that action itself, which is meant here, and thus he presented it in the plural form. His saying: 'If a muhrim applies perfume' - the better reading is 'tayyaba muhrimun' as in most copies of al-Hidayah, because al-tatayyub is transitive, so his word 'udwan' cannot be made an object. It can be said: it is a tamyez from the relation of applying perfume to the muhrim. What is meant by perfume: everything that has a pleasant scent, such as violet, basil, jasmine, roses, and others. His saying: 'a limb' i.e. a complete one like the head, thigh, and others. Al-Kirmani said in his Manasik: If he perfumed all his limbs, he owes one dam because of the unity of category; and if the perfume was on his separate limbs, that is all combined, and if it reaches a complete limb, then he owes a dam, otherwise sadaqah. His saying: 'a limb' - as for a garment most of which is perfumed, it is required for the obligation of dam that he continues wearing it for a day. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His saying: 'with henna' - with kasr of the ha, and with fatha and tashdid of the nun with madd - it is a well-known plant with which women dye their hands and feet, and its color is red. It has been reported in a hadith narrated by al-Bayhaqi with a weak chain: 'Henna is a perfume.' If you say: Why did he single it out for mention while it is included in perfume? I say: Because of the disagreement concerning it. His saying: 'applied oil' - with tashdid of the open daal from al-idhaan.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umda al-Ri'aya on the chapter of offences (janaayaat) related to a person in the state of ihram. The commentator first explains the title 'Bāb al-Jināyāt' (Chapter of Offences) by noting that after discussing the types of muhrim and their general rulings, the author now turns to specific forbidden acts that incur penalties. The word jinaaya (plural janaaya) literally means 'committing a sin' and is used idiomatically for the sinful act itself. The passage then explains the ruling in the matn: if a muhrim applies perfume (tayyib) to a limb—meaning a whole limb such as the head or thigh—then he must offer a dam (a sacrifice). The commentator clarifies the reading, preferring 'tayyaba muhrimun' as in al-Hidayah, and defines tayyib as anything with a pleasant scent, giving examples like violet, basil, jasmine, and roses. The phrase 'a limb' is explained as a complete limb; al-Kirmani is quoted: if a muhrim perfumes all his limbs, one dam suffices, but if he perfumes several limbs separately, the amount is added together; if it reaches a full limb in total, a dam is required; otherwise, sadaqah (charity). For a garment that is mostly perfumed, the dam is only due if the muhrim wears it continuously for a day, as noted from al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The commentator then addresses henna: it is a plant used for dyeing, red in color. A hadith from al-Bayhaqi (though with a weak chain) states 'Henna is a perfume,' which is why henna is treated under the same ruling. The commentator anticipates an objection: since henna is already included under 'perfume', why is it mentioned separately? The answer is that there is disagreement (ikhtilāf) among scholars regarding henna, so it is singled out for clarity. Finally, applying oil (idhān) is also mentioned, with a brief note on the pronunciation. In summary, this passage lays out the rule: any perfuming or dyeing of a full limb by a muhrim incurs a dam; for less than a full limb, sadaqah; and for a perfumed garment, the dam depends on continuous wearing for a day.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, and is therefore subject to specific prohibitions and penalties.
جناية (jināyah): In this context, it refers to an offensive act committed by a muhrim that incurs a penalty (dam or sadaqah).
طيب (tayyib): Perfume or anything with a pleasant scent, including flowers and oils.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required as expiation for certain violations during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what penalty is due if a muhrim applies perfume to an entire limb?
A) A dam (blood sacrifice)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) No penalty if done unintentionally
D) Fasting for three days

Key Takeaway
A muhrim must compensate for perfume on a full limb with a dam; otherwise sadaqah, and a perfumed garment requires continuous wear for a day.

Penalties for Prohibited Acts in Ihram: The Case of Perfume and Oil
Ruling with proof for prohibited acts in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling (dam or sadaqah) for a muḥrim applying perfume, henna, or pure oil, and explain the basis of the disagreement between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Pure olive/sesame oil requires a dam according to Abu Hanifah because it is the base of perfume.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya details the penalties (jinayat) for a muḥrim violating the prohibitions of ihrām. The commentary focuses on the definitions and rulings for applying perfume (ṭīb), dyeing with henna, and applying oil. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises over pure olive and sesame oil: Is it considered a perfume (requiring a dam) or not (requiring only sadaqah)? The commentator explains the reasoning and the positions of Abu Hanifah, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Locate the act being ruled upon: applying perfume to a limb, dyeing with henna, or applying oil. Note how the commentary defines each term (e.g., ṭīb includes any fragrant substance, henna is a specific dye, oil here means pure olive or sesame).
The passage also covers sewn garments, head covering, and shaving; focus on the perfume/oil section for the dispute.
2
Determine the penalty level
The text states the penalty: dam (sacrifice) or sadaqah (charity). For perfume, henna, and perfumed oils, the penalty is always dam. For pure oils, there is disagreement.
Remember: dam is wajib, not fard, because it is compensatory.
3
Follow the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifah rules dam for pure olive/sesame oil. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) rule sadaqah. The commentator gives the reason: these oils are the base of perfumes and remove dishevelment (tafth), thus they are like perfume.
Note the authority: the text presents Abu Hanifah's view first with 'yajibu al-dam', indicating it is the relied-upon position.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i distinguishes: if the oil is applied to hair, dam is due; if to other limbs, nothing. His reasoning is based on adornment (zinah).
The Hanafi response is not explicit but implies that the oil's inherent quality as a perfume base makes location irrelevant.
5
Apply the tarjih (preferred ruling)
The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifah's view: dam for applying pure oil to any limb. This is the position of the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
This shows the principle of tarjih within the school when the Sahibayn differ.

Source Text

باب الجنايات
إن طيب محرم عضواً، أو خَضَبَ رأسَه بِحِنَّاء، أو ادهَن بزيت
[١] قوله : باب الجنايات ؛ لَمَّا ذكر أقسام المحرمين وأحكامهم، شرع في بيان ما يعرض لهم باعتبار الإحرام أو الحرم من الجنايات، وهو جمع جناية - بالكسر - وهو في الأصل مصدر جنى، إذا ارتكب معصية، وشاع استعماله في نفس ذلك الفعل، وهو المراد هاهنا ، ولذا أورده بلفظ : الجمع.
[٢] قوله : إن تطيب محرم ؛ الأولى طيب محرم ، كما في أكثر نسخ «الهداية»، فإنّ التطيّب لازم، فلا يمكن جعل قوله عضواً مفعولاً، ويمكن أن يقال: إنه تمييز من نسبة التطيب إلى المحرم ، والمراد بالطيب : كلّ ما له رائحة طيبة : كالبنفسج والريحان والياسمين والورود وغير ذلك.
[٣]قوله : عضواً ؛ أي كاملاً كالرأس والفخذ وغيرهما ، قال الكرماني في مناسكه»: لو طيب جميع أعضائه فعليه دم واحد لاتحاد الجنس، ولو كان الطيب في أعضائه المتفرقة ، ذلك يجمع كله فإن بلغ عضواً كاملاً فعليه دم، وإلا فصدقة.
[٤] قوله عضواً ؛ وأما الثوب المطيب أكثره فيشترط للزوم الدم فيه دوام لبسه يوماً. كذا في «الدر المختار»).
[0]قوله : بالحناء ؛ - بكسر الحاء ،وبفتحها وتشديد النون مع المد - : وهو نبت معروف يخضب به النساء أيديهن وأرجلهن، ويكون لونه أحمر، وقد ورد في حديث رواه البيهقي بسند ضعيف : «الحناء طيب». فإن قلت : فلم أفرده بالذكر مع دخوله في الطيب. قلت : لمكان الاختلاف فيه.
[٦] قوله : ادهن ؛ بتشديد الدال المفتوحة من الإدهان. أي استعمل الدهن في عضو.
[۲] ثُمَّ الادهانُ إن كان بزيت خالص ، أو بحل خالص يجب الدم عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما تجب الصدقة، وعند الشَّافِعِي) إن استعمله في الشعر يَجِبُ الدم، وإن استعمله في غيره ، فلا شيء عليه، أمَّا الدّهنُ المُطيِّب : كدهنِ البنفسج ، ونحوه ، فيجبُ الدَّمُ اتفاقاً للتَّطيب.
(۲) [0] [۸] (أو ليس مخيطاً ، أو ستر رأسه يوماً ) كاملاً ، أو حلق ربع رأسه (۸)
[١] قوله : أو بحل ؛ - بفتح الحاء المهملة، وتشديد اللام – : هو الشيرج ، يعني دهن السمسم.
[٢] قوله : يجب الدم ؛ لأنّ دهن الزيت والسمسم أصلُ الطيب، باعتبار أنه يلقي فيهما البنفسج والورد وغيرهما، فيصير طيباً، ولا يخلوان عـن نـوع طيب، ويزيلان التفث، ويصلحان الشعر، بخلاف غيرهما من الادهان. كذا في «البحر»

[0] قوله : أو لبس ؛ أي لبساً معتاداً ، فلو ألقى القباء على كتفيه من غير إدخال اليد لا شيء عليه إلا الكراهة.
[٦] قوله : مَخيطاً ؛ - بفتح الميم وكسر الخاء المعجمة – أصله مخيوط.
[٧] قوله : يوماً ؛ أي كاملاً ؛ أي مقداره أو مقدار الليلة الكاملة، وهذا قيد اللبس والستر كليهما.
[۸] قوله : ربع رأسه ؛ وكذا ربع لحيته.
Chapter of Offences. If a muḥrim perfumes a limb, or dyes his head with henna, or applies oil of olive or sesame, or wears a sewn garment, or covers his head for a complete day, or shaves a quarter of his head. [1] His saying: Chapter of Offences; when he mentioned the categories of muḥrims and their rulings, he began to explain what occurs to them due to ihrām or the sanctuary of offences. [2] His saying: If a muḥrim applies perfume; the first is ‘ṭayyiba muḥrim’ as in most copies of al-Hidāyah, for tatayyub is transitive. [3] His saying: a limb; meaning a complete limb like head, thigh, etc. [4] His saying: a limb; regarding a garment most of which is perfumed, the condition for the liability of blood is continuous wearing for a day. [0] His saying: with henna; it is a well-known plant with which women dye hands and feet. [6] His saying: applies oil; from idhān, meaning he used oil on a limb. [2] Then applying oil: if with pure olive oil or pure sesame oil, blood is obligatory according to Abū Ḥanīfah, and according to the two companions, charity is obligatory, and according to al-Shāfiʿī: if he uses it on hair, blood is obligatory; if on other than hair, nothing is due. As for perfumed oil, like violet oil, blood is obligatory by agreement due to perfuming. [8] (Or wears a sewn garment, or covers his head for a complete day, or shaves a quarter of his head.) [1] His saying: or sesame oil; it is sesame oil. [2] His saying: blood is obligatory; because olive and sesame oil are the base of perfume. [3] His saying: obligatory; based on it not being perfume. [4] His saying: nothing is due; as nothing is due by agreement if he does not use it for perfuming. [0] His saying: or wears; normal wearing. [6] His saying: sewn; originally makhīyūṭ. [7] His saying: a day; complete day or complete night. [8] His saying: quarter of his head; and similarly quarter of his beard.
Source pages p. 613

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqāyah explains the chapter on offences (jināyāt) committed by a person in ihrām. It begins by defining jināyah as committing a sin, and here it refers to prohibited acts during ihrām. The first ruling: if a muḥrim applies perfume (ṭīb) to a complete limb (like head or thigh), he owes a dam (blood sacrifice). If he perfumes multiple limbs, they are combined; if it reaches the extent of a whole limb, a dam is due; otherwise, sadaqah. For a garment that is mostly perfumed, continuous wearing for a day is required for liability. Henna is specifically mentioned because there is disagreement (whether it is considered perfume). For applying oil: pure olive or sesame oil trigger a dam according to Abū Ḥanīfah, but only sadaqah according to Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad (the Ṣāḥibayn). Al-Shāfiʿī distinguishes: if used on hair, dam; otherwise nothing. Perfumed oils like violet oil require a dam by agreement. The reason given is that olive and sesame oils are the base for perfumes and remove dishevelment. The commentary clarifies that if the oil is used for medical purposes (not adornment), nothing is due. Next, wearing a sewn garment: normal wearing (like inserting arms) triggers liability; merely throwing over shoulders without inserting arms is only disliked. Covering the head for a full day (or night) requires a dam. Shaving a quarter of the head or beard requires a dam. These rulings are based on analogical reasoning (qiyās) and the principle that such acts violate the state of ihrām.

Key Terms
طيب (ṭīb): Perfume: anything with a pleasant scent, such as violet, basil, jasmine, roses, etc.
حناء (ḥinnā’): Henna: a plant used for dyeing, with a red color; it is considered a type of perfume according to a weak hadith.
ادهان (idhān): Applying oil (to the body or hair).
مخيط (makhīṭ): Sewn garment: any garment that is tailored and sewn, such as a shirt or pants.
دم (dam): Blood: a sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as a penalty for violating a prohibition of ihrām.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity: here it refers to giving a specific amount (e.g., half a sā‘ of wheat) as a lesser penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does henna receive separate mention in the text even though it is a type of perfume?
A) Because henna is not actually a perfume.
B) Because there is disagreement about its ruling.
C) Because henna is only used by women.
D) Because the hadith about henna is weak.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a dam for applying perfume, henna, or any oil that is either perfumed or, according to Abu Hanifah, a base of perfume (like olive/sesame) to a muḥrim, unless used purely for medical purposes.
