Hajj Jinaayat: Actions Requiring Dam and the Principle of Tadakhul
Commentary on Hajj jinayat incurring dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the actions during Hajj that require dam and explain the Hanafi principle of tadakhul (merging) as applied to nail trimming.

Core Idea
Dam is wajib for specified violations in ihram; the principle of tadakhul merges multiple similar violations into one compensation unless kafarah intervenes.

In this lesson, we examine the chapter of jinayat (offenses) in Hajj from the Hanafi tradition. The commentary on the matn lists specific actions that incur dam, such as shaving certain body hair, trimming nails, and performing tawaf in a state of impurity. A key intra-Hanafi dispute emerges regarding whether multiple sittings of nail trimming require separate dam or merge into one. This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya elucidates these rulings and the underlying principle of tadakhul.

Guided Path
1
List the actions requiring dam
Go through the passage and identify each action mentioned: shaving specific body parts, trimming nails, performing tawaf in janabah/hadath, leaving Arafat before the Imam, and abandoning parts of tawaf, sa'i, or stoning.
Not all actions are equally familiar; focus on the ones discussed in detail.
2
Distinguish shaving rules by body part
Note that for the head and beard, shaving a quarter suffices for dam, but for other parts (armpit, pubic region, etc.), shaving the entire area is required. The reasoning involves customary practice.
This distinction is based on 'urf (custom), not on the sacredness of the part.
3
Analyze the nail trimming dispute
The passage explains that Imam Muhammad holds that multiple sittings of nail trimming merge into one dam if no kafarah intervened, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf require separate dam for each sitting involving a hand or foot.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf based on the principle of tadakhul.
4
Understand tawaf impurity rulings
Distinguish between tawaf al-fard (obligatory) and other tawafs. Only janabah (major impurity) triggers dam for non-fard tawafs; for tawaf al-fard, even minor impurity (hadath) incurs dam. Impurity on clothing is only makruh.
The hierarchy of tawaf types affects the severity of the offense.
5
Identify other violations
Leaving Arafat before the Imam (i.e., before sunset), abandoning most of tawaf al-ziyarah, tawaf al-sadr, sa'i, standing at Muzdalifah, or stoning all require dam.
These are listed but not elaborated; they follow similar reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الجناية
أو محاجمه، أو إحدى إبطيه، أو عانته، أو رقبته، أو قص أظفار يديه، ورجليه في مجلس واحد (1)، أو يد، أو رجل، أو طاف للقدوم، أو للصدرِ جُنُباً أو للفرض محدثاً. أو أفاض من عرفة قبل الإمام ، أو ترك أقل سبع الفرض، وبتركِ أكثره بقي محرماً حتى يطوفه، أو طواف الصدر أو للفرض محدثاً.
قوله : أو محاجمه ؛ هذا وما بعده معطوف على ربع رأسه : أي حلق محاجمه، وهو جمع المحجم، وهو موضع الحجامة، أو حلق إحدى إبطيه، أو حلق عانته أو رقبته، فيعتبر فيها حلق الكل لا الربع ؛ لأنّ العادة لم تجر فيها بالاقتصار على البعض، فلا يكون حلق البعض اتفاقاً كاملاً، بخلاف حلق ربع الرأس واللحية، فإنه معتاد لبعض الناس. كذا في «البحر»(2).
[٢] قوله : إبطيه ; أو حلق شعر الصدر أو الساق أو الركبة أو الفخذ أو العضد أو الساعد. كذا في «اللباب»(3).
[٣] قوله : في مجلس واحد ; وكذا إذا تعدد المجلس ; لأن مبنى هذه الكفّارة على التداخل، إلا إذا تخللت الكفّارة، هذا على قول محمد الله، وأما عندهما فتجبُ أربعة دماء إذا قص في كل مجلس يداً أو رجلاً. كذا في «الهداية»(4).
(٤) قوله : أو يد أو رجل ; أي إن قص أظافير رجل واحدة أو يد واحدة، يجب الدم إقامة للربع، مقام الكل، كما في حلق الرأس.
[0] قوله : أو طاف للقدوم ... الخ ; الأصلُ فيه : أنّ طواف الفرض أقوى من الطواف الواجب، وفي حكمه الطواف المسنون والنفل ، كطواف القدوم، فإنه يجب بالشروع، فأداء طواف الفرض محدثاً من غير طهارة أخرى جناية قوية، فتجب فيها الدم، بخلاف طواف الصدر والقدوم ، فإنّ انتفاء الطهارة الصغرى فيه لا يجب به دم، بل إذا طاف به جنباً بانتفاء الطهارة الكبرى فحينئذ يجب الدم.
[١] قوله : محدثاً ; وأما الطواف مع نجاسةِ الثوب والبدن فمكروه فقط. كذا في «البحر» (1)
[٢] قوله : قبل الإمام ; المراد به قبل الغروب، لأنّ الإمام يجب عليه النفر بعد الغروب، فلو غربت الشمس ونفروا ولم ينفر الإمامُ لا شيء عليهم، ولو نفر الإمامُ قبل غروب الشمس وتابعوه كان عليه وعليهم الدم. كذا في «البحر »(2)
[٣] قوله : أقل سبع ; - بفتح السين - وإضافته لامية، والفرض بمعنى المفروض : أي ترك أقل من سبع دورات الطواف المفروض، وهو طواف الزيارة.
[٤]قوله : بقي محرماً ; فإن رجع إلى أهله فعليه حتماً أن يعود بذلك الإحرام ويطوف بقية الأشواط ، ولا يجزئ عنه البدل.
[0] قوله : أو أكثر ; لأنه يعد تاركاً للركن ; لأن للأكثر حكم الكل.
[٦] قوله : أو طواف الصدر ; هذا وما بعده إلى قوله : «أو حلق» ; معطوف على قوله : «أقل»: أي تركُ طواف الوداع كلّه أو أكثره، وهو أربعة أشواط منه، أو ترك السعي كل أو أكثره، أو ترك الوقوف بجمع : أي مزدلفة ليلة النحر، أو ترك الرمي كله في جميع الأيام، أو ترك الرمي كله في يوم واحد من أيام الرمي، أو ترك أكثر الرمي الأول وهو رمي يوم النحر، ففي هذه الصور يجب دم.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Jinaya.
Or his cupping places, or one of his armpits, or his pubic region, or his neck, or trimming the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand, or a foot, or he performed tawaf for arrival or for departure while in a state of janabah, or for the obligatory tawaf while in a state of hadath. Or he departed from Arafat before the Imam, or he left less than seven circuits of the obligatory tawaf, and by leaving its majority he remains in ihram until he performs it, or the tawaf al-sadr or for the obligatory tawaf while in a state of hadath.
His statement: 'or his cupping places' – this and what follows are conjoined to 'quarter of his head': meaning shaving his cupping places, which is the plural of mahjam, which is the place of cupping, or shaving one of his armpits, or shaving his pubic region or his neck. In these, shaving all is considered, not a quarter, because custom does not apply to limiting to part, so shaving part is not a complete convention, unlike shaving a quarter of the head and beard, for it is customary for some people. Thus in 'al-Bahr' (2).
[2] His statement: 'his armpits' – or shaving the hair of the chest, leg, knee, thigh, upper arm, or forearm. Thus in 'al-Lubab' (3).
[3] His statement: 'in one sitting' – and likewise if the sittings are multiple, because the basis of this expiation is merging, unless the expiation is interposed. This is according to the saying of Muhammad, may Allah be pleased with him. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?), four bloods are obligatory if he trimmed in each sitting a hand or a foot. Thus in 'al-Hidaya' (4).
(4) His statement: 'or a hand or a foot' – meaning if he trimmed the nails of one foot or one hand, the blood is obligatory as a quarter is considered in place of the whole, as in shaving the head.
[0] His statement: 'or he performed tawaf for arrival...' – the principle of this is that the obligatory tawaf is stronger than the wajib tawaf, and in its ruling is the sunnah and nafl tawaf, like tawaf al-qudum, for it becomes obligatory by starting it. Performing the obligatory tawaf while in a state of hadath without another purification is a strong offense, so blood is due for it, unlike tawaf al-sadr and al-qudum, for the absence of minor purity does not obligate blood, but if he performs it while junub due to absence of major purity, then blood is due.
[1] His statement: 'while in a state of hadath' – and as for tawaf with impurity on the clothing or body, it is only makruh. Thus in 'al-Bahr' (1).
[2] His statement: 'before the Imam' – the meaning is before sunset, because the Imam must depart after sunset. So if the sun set and they departed and the Imam did not depart, nothing is upon them. And if the Imam departed before sunset and they followed him, blood is due from him and them. Thus in 'al-Bahr' (2).
[3] His statement: 'less than seven' – with a fatha on the sin, and its idafah is lamyyah, and al-fard means the obligatory: meaning he left less than seven rounds of the obligatory tawaf, which is tawaf al-ziyarah.
[4] His statement: 'he remains in ihram' – for if he returns to his family, he must absolutely return with that ihram and perform the remaining circuits, and a substitute does not suffice for him.
[0] His statement: 'or more' – because he is considered abandoner of the pillar; for the majority has the ruling of the whole.
[6] His statement: 'or tawaf al-sadr' – this and what follows up to his statement 'or shaving' are conjoined to his statement 'less': meaning leaving the farewell tawaf entirely or most of it, which is four circuits thereof, or leaving the sa'i entirely or most of it, or leaving the standing at Jam' i.e. Muzdalifah on the night of sacrifice, or leaving the stoning entirely on all days, or leaving the stoning entirely on one day of the days of stoning, or leaving most of the first stoning which is the stoning of the Day of Sacrifice. In these cases, blood is due.
Source pages p. 615

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of jinayat (offenses) in Hajj, listing various violations that incur a blood offering (dam). The base text (matn) enumerates actions: shaving body hair (cupping places, armpits, pubic region, neck), trimming nails in one sitting or even a single hand/foot, performing tawaf in a state of major impurity (janabah) for arrival or departure tawaf, or performing obligatory tawaf while in minor impurity (hadath). It also includes leaving Arafat before the Imam, skipping most of the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah), and abandoning the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr). The commentary, from 'Umda al-Ri'aya, elaborates on each phrase. For shaving, it notes that unlike the head (where a quarter can merit penalty), for these body parts, shaving the entire area is required due to custom. For nail trimming, a key intra-Hanafi dispute is highlighted: Imam Muhammad holds that multiple sittings merge into one dam unless a kafarah (expiation) intervenes, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf obligate separate bloods for each sitting where a limb is trimmed. Regarding tawaf, the commentary distinguishes between obligatory (fard), wajib, and sunnah tawafs: performing obligatory tawaf without wudu or ghusl incurs a dam, but for sunnah tawaf (qudum, sadr), only janabah triggers dam, not mere hadath. Impurity on clothes or body is only makruh, not penalized. Departing Arafat before the Imam (before sunset) also necessitates dam. Leaving less than seven circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah leaves one in ihram, requiring completion; leaving most (four or more) is like abandoning the pillar. Similarly, abandoning most of tawaf al-sadr, sa'i, standing at Muzdalifah, or stoning (all or most on a day) incurs dam. The passage thus provides a comprehensive list of hajj violations and their compensations.

Key Terms
دم (dam): Blood offering (sacrifice of a sheep or equivalent) required as penalty for certain violations during Hajj.
طواف الفرض (tawaf al-fard): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba, i.e., tawaf al-ziyarah (tawaf of visitation), which is a pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a pilgrim trims his nails of his hands in one sitting and his feet in a separate sitting without offering any kafarah in between, how many dam are required?
A) One dam
B) Two dam
C) Four dam
D) No dam

Key Takeaway
Dam is wajib for specific violations during Hajj, and the principle of tadakhul (merging) applies to multiple similar violations according to Imam Muhammad's view.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Actions That Obligate a Blood Sacrifice (Dam) in Hajj
Listing of Hajj violations requiring dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which omissions during Hajj require a dam and identify the exception for minor impurity in Tawaf al-Qudum and Tawaf al-Sadr.

Core Idea
Leaving most of any wajib act in Hajj requires a dam; minor impurity in Tawaf al-Qudum/Sadr is excepted.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah enumerates the major omissions and violations during Hajj that incur a dam (blood sacrifice). Understanding this list is crucial for pilgrims to know when they must offer compensation. The commentary clarifies nuances, such as the effect of majority and the distinction between major and minor impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed acts requiring dam
Scan the passage to list all acts for which a dam is obligatory. These include: performing obligatory tawaf with minor impurity, departing Arafat before the Imam, leaving less than seven circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (and leaving most of it), leaving the farewell tawaf, leaving sa'y, leaving standing at Muzdalifah, leaving all or most of the stoning, and shaving the head outside the Haram for Hajj or Umrah.
The list continues on page 617 with additional items.
2
Apply the 'majority rule'
For many acts, leaving most of the act has the same ruling as leaving the entire act. For example, leaving four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah means the pilgrim remains in ihram until completion and must offer a dam.
The text states 'إذا ترك أربعة أشواط أو أكثر بقي محرماً حتى يطوف'.
3
Distinguish impurity types for tawaf
Minor impurity (e.g., without wudu) in Tawaf al-Qudum and Tawaf al-Sadr does not require dam, only major impurity (janabah) does. Impurity on the garment or body is merely makruh.
This exception is explicitly stated: 'بخلاف طواف الصدر والقدوم'.
4
Note the exception for a Mu'tamir
A Mu'tamir who leaves the Haram without exiting ihram and then returns to shave inside the Haram does not owe dam. This is because the act (shaving) was performed in its proper place.
The passage says 'لا في معتمر رَجَعَ من حلّ، ثُمَّ قَصْرَ'.

[The commentary on Al-Hidayah:] Or [he performed] the obligatory [tawaf] while in a state of minor impurity. Or he departed from Arafat before the Imam. Or he left less than seven [circuits] of the obligatory [tawaf]; and by leaving most of it, he remains in ihram until he performs it. Or [he left] the farewell tawaf. And [the ruling:] blood sacrifice is required. Contrary to the farewell and arrival tawaf, in which the absence of minor purity does not necessitate a blood sacrifice; rather, if he performs it while in major impurity, then blood sacrifice becomes necessary. [1] His statement: 'in a state of minor impurity' — and performing tawaf with impurity on the garment or body is only makruh. (Al-Bahr) [2] His statement: 'before the Imam' — meaning before sunset, because the Imam must depart after sunset. If the sun set and they departed while the Imam did not, there is no penalty on them. If the Imam departed before sunset and they followed him, then both he and they owe a blood sacrifice. (Al-Bahr) [3] His statement: 'less than seven' — meaning fewer than seven circuits of the obligatory tawaf, which is the tawaf of visiting (Tawaf al-Ziyarah). [4] His statement: 'he remains in ihram' — if he returns to his family, he must definitely return with that ihram and perform the remaining circuits, and a substitute is not acceptable. [0] His statement: 'or more' — because he is considered a performer of the pillar; the majority has the ruling of the whole. [6] His statement: 'or the farewell tawaf' — this and what follows up to his statement 'or shaving' are connected to his statement 'less' [in the list]. That is: leaving the farewell tawaf entirely or most of it (four circuits), leaving the sa'y entirely or most of it, leaving the standing at Jam' (Muzdalifah) on the night of sacrifice, leaving all the stoning in all of the days, leaving all the stoning on a single day of the days of stoning, or leaving most of the first stoning (stoning of the day of Nahr) — in these cases, a blood sacrifice is obligatory. (Al-Bahr al-Raiq, 3:19; 3:25) [On page 617:] The book of Hajj, chapter of violations. [1] [Commentary:] Or four from it, or the sa'y, or the standing at Jam', or all the stoning, or on a single day, or the first stoning, or most of it — meaning the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr. Or shaving in the Halal for Hajj or Umrah — because shaving is specific to Mina, which is part of the Haram. [Exception:] Not for a Mu'tamir who returned from the Halal then shortened. [Footnote:] (1) His statement: 'or the first stoning' — although this is covered by his statement 'or on a single day', it is mentioned explicitly following the author of Al-Hidayah due to its importance. If one leaves stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the remaining days, charity is owed, not blood sacrifice, because it is the least of stoning in those days, unlike the day of Nahr where it constitutes all of the stoning. [2] His statement: 'or shaving' — the summary: if he shaves his head or shortens his hair to exit ihram for Hajj or Umrah outside the Haram, a blood sacrifice is obligatory, because shaving and similar acts are specific to a particular place, namely the Haram for both, and the time for shaving in Hajj is also specified to the days of Nahr. [3] His statement: 'Halal' — meaning outside the Haram. [4] His statement: 'not for a Mu'tamir' — no blood sacrifice is obligatory for a Mu'tamir who went out to the Halal without exiting ihram, then returned to the Haram and shaved or shortened there. (Ghayat al-Hukkam, etc.)
Source pages p. 616

Commentary
This passage from the commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah lists the major omissions and violations during Hajj that incur a wajib dam (blood sacrifice). It covers: performing obligatory tawaf with minor impurity (though major impurity requires dam), departing Arafat before the Imam, leaving less than seven circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (and remaining in ihram if more than half is left), and leaving Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell). It clarifies that for Tawaf al-Qudum and al-Sadr, minor impurity does not necessitate dam, only major impurity does. The list continues on page 617: leaving four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, leaving all or most of Sa'y, standing at Muzdalifah, all ramy (stoning), ramy on one day, or the first ramy (stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah) or most of it. Also shaving the head in the Halal (outside the Haram) for Hajj or Umrah requires dam, because shaving is restricted to the Haram. An exception is a Mu'tamir who leaves the Haram without exiting ihram and then returns to shave inside the Haram—no dam. The commentary relies on 'Al-Bahr al-Raiq' and 'Al-Hidayah'. This is a straightforward enumeration; the key point is that the majority of an act has the ruling of the whole, so leaving most of any wajib incurs dam.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Ka'bah performed after returning from Mina on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell circumambulation (Tawaf al-Wada') performed before leaving Makkah after Hajj.
الرمي (ar-Ramy): Stoning the three pillars (Jamarat) at Mina during the days of Tashriq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a pilgrim leaves four circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, what is the ruling?
A) He only owes one dam and the Hajj is valid.
B) He remains in ihram and must complete the remaining circuits; dam is due.
C) He must perform a new Hajj the following year.
D) No penalty, as four is not the majority.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a blood sacrifice (dam) for leaving most or all of any wajib act of Hajj, except for minor impurity in non-obligatory tawaf.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Actions Necessitating Dam in Hajj and Umrah
Lists violations requiring dam with refined exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific violations in Hajj/Umrah that require a dam and explain the conditions and exceptions based on location, timing, and intent.

Core Idea
A dam is wajib for specific violations; shaving outside the Haram and intimate acts with desire require it even without emission.

This passage from the chapter on Hajj offenses (Bab al-Jinaya) enumerates the violations that obligate a dam (blood sacrifice) as expiation. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah refines the rulings by clarifying nuances such as the exception for a mu'tamir who returns to the Haram before tahallul, and the difference of opinion on the number of dams for shaving outside after the Days of Nahr. Understanding these details ensures correct application of the penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
For each violation listed, determine whether it occurs in Hajj or Umrah, and note the specific ritual involved (tawaf, sa'i, wuquf, ramy, halq, taqbil, etc.).
The same act may have different rulings in Hajj vs. Umrah (e.g., timing restrictions for shaving only apply to Hajj).
2
Determine the location factor
Check whether the act was performed inside the Haram (sanctuary) or outside (hill). Shaving and hair shortening are location-specific: dam is due only if done outside the Haram, except for the mu'tamir exception.
The exception: a mu'tamir who leaves the Haram before tahallul, returns, and then shortens inside the Haram owes no dam.
3
Apply the timing factor
For Hajj, shaving and tawaf al-ifadah have time restrictions (Days of Nahr). Delaying beyond these days incurs a dam; if the pilgrim shaves outside after the days, two dams are due per Abu Hanifah.
The time factor does not apply to Umrah for shaving or tawaf.
4
Analyze the nature of the act
Kissing or touching with desire takes the same ruling as intercourse for dam, even without emission. This is because such acts are precursors (dawa'i) to intercourse.
Acts without desire (e.g., accidental touch) or masturbation without emission do not require dam.
5
Note intra-Hanafi differences
Abu Hanifah holds that shaving outside the Haram after the Days of Nahr requires two dams; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani may require one dam. The mufta bihi follows the text as per Al-Hidayah.
This difference affects the penalty in practice; the relied-upon view is two dams.

The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses: Or four [circuits] from it, or the Sa'i, or standing at Muzdalifah, or all of the stoning, or on one day, or the first stoning, or most of it, or shaving in the halal [area] for Hajj or Umrah, not for a performer of Umrah who returned from the halal then shortened [his hair]. Statement: 'or the first stoning'... Statement: 'or shaving'... Statement: 'halal'... Statement: 'not for a performer of Umrah'... Or kissing, or touching with desire whether he emitted or not, or delaying the shaving, or the obligatory Tawaf beyond the days of Nahr, or advancing one ritual before another. That is, if the performer of Umrah left the Haram before tahallul, then returned, and shortened, nothing is upon him. It is specified to the Umrah performer because the Hajj pilgrim, if he leaves the Haram before tahallul, then returns to the Haram, the blood sacrifice becomes obligatory upon him. Or kissing... Know that his statement 'or kissing' is not coordinated with his statement 'shortened'; rather it is coordinated with his statement 'or shaving in the halal'. Or delaying the shaving... Or advancing one ritual before another... Statement: 'specified'... Statement: 'the blood sacrifice becomes obligatory upon him'... Statement: 'or kissing'... Statement: 'know...' Statement: 'or delayed'... Statement: 'ritual'... So if the days of Nahr have passed and he shaved outside the Haram, two blood sacrifices are upon him according to Abu Hanifah.
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on offenses in Hajj (Bab al-Jinaya). It lists various actions during Hajj or Umrah that necessitate a dam (blood sacrifice) as a penalty for violation. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the scope and conditions of each ruling. 

The base text enumerates that omitting or delaying certain rituals—like performing only four circuits of Tawaf or less, leaving out Sa'i, missing Wuquf at Muzdalifah, not stoning all or most of the jamarat, stoning on only one day, missing the first stoning (Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr), shaving the head outside the Haram for Hajj or Umrah—all require a dam. However, an exception is made for a mu'tamir who leaves the Haram before tahallul (partial release from Ihram) and then returns and shortens his hair; no dam is required. 

The commentary then elaborates: The first stoning is singled out because missing it on other days only requires sadaqah, not a dam, since it is a lesser stoning. Shaving outside the Haram obligates a dam because shaving is specific to the Haram; for Hajj, it is also time-specific to the Days of Nahr. A mu'tamir who leaves and returns without having done tahallul and then shaves inside the Haram has no penalty. 

The passage continues with more actions: kissing or touching with desire (with or without ejaculation), delaying shaving or the obligatory Tawaf beyond the Days of Nahr, and performing rituals out of order (e.g., shaving before stoning). For kissing and touching, the commentary notes that these take the same ruling as intercourse because they are its precursors—dam is due even without emission. For delaying, it clarifies that if the pilgrim returns after the Days of Nahr and shaves in the Haram, no dam is due; but if he shaves outside after the Days, two dams are required per Abu Hanifah. Finally, 'nusuk' (ritual) means any act of worship in Hajj, and the prohibition is on advancing what must be delayed or vice versa. The relied-upon fatwa follows these details as established in Hanafi sources like Al-Hidayah and later commentaries.

Key Terms
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (slaughtering a sheep or goat) as expiation for violating a wajib or committing an offense during Hajj/Umrah.
حل (hill): The area outside the Haram (sanctuary) of Makkah.
نسك (nusuk): A ritual act of worship in Hajj or Umrah, such as shaving, stoning, tawaf, etc.
معتمر (mu'tamir): A person performing Umrah (the lesser pilgrimage).
تقبيل (taqbil): Kissing one's spouse with sexual desire while in Ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a mu'tamir who leaves the Haram before tahallul, returns, and then shaves inside the Haram?
A) He must offer a dam.
B) He must offer two dams.
C) No penalty is required.
D) He must offer sadaqah.

Key Takeaway
Dam is obligatory for specific violations of Hajj/Umrah wajibat; location, timing, and intent are decisive factors, and the mufta bihi for shaving outside after days of Nahr is two dams per Abu Hanifah.

Dam for Ihram Violations: Obligations and the Qarin Dispute
Commentary on rulings of dam for ihram violations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ihram violations that require dam and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the number of dams for a qarin who shaves before sacrificing.

Core Idea
Dam is wajib for specified ihram violations; the qarin's shaving before sacrifice triggers an ikhtilaf: two dams (Abu Hanifa) vs. one (Sahibayn).

This passage from a Hanafi commentary on al-Hidayah outlines the obligations of dam (blood sacrifice) for various violations during ihram. It then delves into a specific dispute: how many dams does a qarin owe if he shaves his head before slaughtering? You will learn the list of violations, the general principle of dam, and the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf that later authorities resolved in favor of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
List the violations requiring dam
Identify from the text the specific acts that trigger a dam obligation: kissing, touching with desire (with or without ejaculation), delaying shaving beyond the days of al-Nahr, delaying the obligatory tawaf beyond those days, and advancing one ritual before another.
Also note the distinction between hajj pilgrim and mu'tamir for leaving the sanctuary.
2
Understand the dam obligation
The text states 'fa-lahu dam' – a sheep must be slaughtered as compensation. The commentary from al-Lubab emphasizes that ignorance, forgetfulness, coercion, etc., do not exempt one from this wajib.
Dam is wajib at the level of obligation but not fard because it can be compensated.
3
Distinguish hajj and umrah timing
The commentary clarifies that for mu'tamir, shaving and tawaf are not time-bound, so delaying them incurs no penalty. For hajj pilgrims, these acts must be completed within the days of al-Nahr.
Similarly, leaving the sanctuary before tahlul triggers dam for hajj but not for umrah.
4
Analyze the qarin case and ikhtilaf
The qarin who shaves before sacrificing: Abu Hanifa holds two dams are due (one for advancing shaving, one for delaying sacrifice). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold one dam suffices (the dam of Qiran already covers the combination).
The commentators correct the initial text of al-Hidayah, stating that Abu Hanifa's two dams consist of one for the combined violation and one for Qiran.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities (authors of al-Fath, al-Kifayah, al-Inayah) adopt the Sahibayn's view: one dam. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Thus, a qarin who shaves before sacrifice owes only the dam of Qiran.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling commentary from a Hanafi fiqh work (likely a sharh of al-Hidayah). It covers various violations in ihram that necessitate offering a dam (blood sacrifice). The author begins by listing specific actions that trigger the obligation: kissing, touching with desire (whether ejaculation occurs or not), delaying the shaving of the head beyond the days of al-Nahr (the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah), delaying the obligatory circumambulation (tawaf al-ifadah or tawaf al-ziyarah) past the days of al-Nahr, and advancing one ritual before another (e.g., shaving before slaughtering). The commentary clarifies that these rulings apply differently to the mu'tamir (one performing Umrah) and the hajj pilgrim. For instance, if a mu'tamir leaves the sanctuary before tahlul (full release) and then returns and shortens his hair, nothing is due; but for a hajj pilgrim in the same situation, a dam is required. Similarly, shaving for the mu'tamir is not time-bound, so delaying it incurs no penalty. The author then notes a grammatical point: the word 'or kissing' is not linked to 'shortened' but to 'shaved'. After listing the violations, the text states 'so he must offer dam' (fa-lahu dam), indicating that any of these acts require a sheep as a sacrifice. The commentary from al-Lubab emphasizes that ignorance, forgetfulness, coercion, etc., do not exempt one from the dam. Finally, a specific case is addressed: a qarin (one who intends both Hajj and Umrah together) who shaves his head before sacrificing. According to Abu Hanifa, he must offer two dams: one for shaving before its time and one for delaying the sacrifice. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (ash-Shibani) hold that only one dam is required. The commentators clarify that the second dam in Abu Hanifa's view is for the combination of advancing and delaying, not two separate penalties.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as compensation for certain violations in ihram.
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim who performs Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, which is part of the tahlul (release from ihram).

The Qarin's Two Dams: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Shaving Before Sacrifice
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam liability for order violation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the number of dams owed by a qarin who shaves before his sacrifice, and explain the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A qarin who shaves before sacrifice owes one penalty dam, not two; the other dam is the dam of Qur'an.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya delves into a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how many compensatory sacrifices (dams) does a qarin (pilgrim combining Hajj and Umrah) owe if he shaves his head before offering the sacrifice on the Day of Nahr? The base text states two dams according to Abu Hanifa, and one according to the Sahibayn. The commentary clarifies that the correct relied-upon view is that only one is a penalty; the other is the dam of Qur'an which is already obligatory on the qarin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's basis
Understand that the ruling concerns the sequence of actions on the Day of Nahr (stoning, sacrifice, shaving, tawaf). The order among the first three is wajib.
For a qarin, the order is required; breaking it triggers a dam.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that two separate dams are due: one for shaving before its proper time (advance) and one for delaying the sacrifice after shaving (postponement).
He treats both deviations as independent violations.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that only one dam is due for the advance (shaving before sacrifice). They do not consider the delay an additional violation.
They view the order as a single wajib; violating it once incurs only one dam.
4
Understand the later verification
Later scholars (e.g., author of al-Bahr) explain that even according to Abu Hanifa, one of the two dams is actually the dam of Qur'an (required for combining Hajj and Umrah), not a penalty. Thus, the practical difference reduces.
The mufta bihi position is that only one penalty dam is due.
5
Apply the practical consequence
A qarin who shaves before his sacrifice must offer only one penalty dam (for the violation of order) in addition to the dam of Qur'an. Total: two dams, but only one as a penalty.
This prevents overburdening the pilgrim with unnecessary penalties.

Source Text

Rather, the correct view is that for delay and advance, one dam is required according to him (Abu Hanifa), and the other is the dam of Qur'an, so not both are penalty dams, rather one is and the other is a dam of gratitude. And according to the two (Sahibayn), since no dam is required for advancing one ritual over another and delaying it, one dam remains, which is the dam of Qur'an. This is the verification of the author of al-Bahr and his student in Manh al-Ghaffar.]
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of dams required for a qarin who shaves before his sacrifice. The author first states the ruling: if a muhrim perfumes a limb, he owes a dam (فَعَلَيْهِ دَم). Then, he mentions the case of a qarin who shaves before sacrificing (فَيَجِبُ دَمَانِ عَلَى قَارِنٍ إِنْ حَلَقَ قَبْلَ ذَبْحِهِ). According to Abu Hanifa, two dams are due: one for shaving before its proper time, and one for delaying the sacrifice after shaving. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), only one dam is due, which is the first (i.e., for shaving before its time). The commentary then explains the sequence of actions on the Day of Nahr: stoning, sacrificing, shaving, and circumambulation. The order among the first three is obligatory (wajib), and breaking it requires a dam for the qarin and mutamatti'. For the mufrid (performing Hajj only), only stoning and shaving are ordered. Circumambulation has no required order; doing it early is merely disliked. The commentary elaborates that the dam is a sheep, and one-seventh of a camel may suffice according to the majority. It also notes that the obligation of dam applies universally regardless of intent, knowledge, or volition. The dispute is then clarified: the Sahibayn hold that only one dam is due for the advance (shaving before stoning or sacrifice), while the postponement (delaying sacrifice) does not incur an additional dam. Abu Hanifa holds that both advance and delay incur separate dams. However, some later scholars (like the author of al-Bahr) argue that the two dams in Abu Hanifa's view are not both penalty dams; one is for the violation of order (jinaayah) and the other is the dam of Qur'an (shukr), which is not a penalty. According to the Sahibayn, since no dam is required for advancing or delaying rituals, the only dam remaining is the dam of Qur'an (which the qarin owes for combining Hajj and Umrah). This passage shows how the Hanafi school has nuanced positions even among its founders, and how later scholars refined the understanding.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A compensatory sacrifice (slaughtering a sheep or one-seventh of a camel) required for certain violations during ihram or for combining Hajj and Umrah.
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim who enters ihram with the intention of performing both Umrah and Hajj together without separating them.
عندهم (indahuma): According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), i.e., the Sahibayn, who differ from Abu Hanifa in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, how many penalty dams does a qarin owe if he shaves before his sacrifice?
A) One
B) Two
C) None (the dam of Qur'an covers it)
D) Three

Key Takeaway
A qarin who violates the wajib order on the Day of Nahr by shaving before his sacrifice owes only one penalty dam; the other dam is the dam of Qur'an, not an additional penalty.

Minor Hajj Violations Requiring Sadaqah
List of minor violations requiring sadaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five violations that require sadaqah during ihram and state the threshold that distinguishes sadaqah from dam.

Core Idea
Minor violations (less than full limb, less than day, less than quarter head, fewer than five nails) require sadaqah, not dam.

Not every violation of ihram requires a full sacrificial animal (dam). For lesser infractions—such as using perfume on only part of a limb or clipping a few nails—a simple charity (sadaqah) suffices. This lesson anchors the precise thresholds that separate sadaqah from dam, a key for both memory and application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five listed acts
Read the passage carefully and note each act: perfuming less than a limb, covering the head, wearing stitched clothing for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, and clipping fewer than five nails.
These acts are all partial transgressions.
2
Understand the threshold principle
For each act, a specific quantity marks the boundary: full limb vs. less, full day vs. less, quarter head vs. less, five nails vs. fewer. If the act reaches or exceeds the limit, a dam is required; otherwise, sadaqah.
The principle of 'complete enjoyment contrary to tafath' triggers dam.
3
Connect to the general rule
The commentary states a general rule: leaving a wajib or committing complete enjoyment (taraffuq kaamil) requires dam; partial acts require sadaqah. Apply this to each listed case.
This rule helps extend the list to other similar violations.
4
Memorise the details
Commit to memory the specific acts and their thresholds. Use the mnemonic: 'less limb, head covering, half day shave, quarter hair, four nails' (incorrect but memorable).
Accuracy is crucial for fatwa and exam.

And if he perfumes less than a limb, or covers his head, or wears stitched clothing for less than a day, or shaves less than a quarter of his head, or clips fewer than five nails. [1] His statement: 'And if he perfumes less than a limb': this together with what is conjuncted is a condition, and its answer is his coming statement: 'he gives in charity half a sa', etc. This is the beginning of mentioning violations for which a dam is not obligatory but rather sadaqah. Commentary
This passage introduces a set of minor violations during ihram that do not require a full dam (sacrificial animal) but only sadaqah (charity). The list includes: using perfume on less than a full limb, covering the head, wearing stitched clothing for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, and clipping fewer than five nails. The commentary explains that these are acts of incomplete enjoyment or minor omissions. The general principle (أَصْل فِي هَذَا الْبَاب) is that any violation involving the abandonment of a wajib of Hajj or full indulgence in comfort (taraffuq kaamil) that contradicts tafath (the state of leaving ihram) requires a dam. Violations that do not reach this level require sadaqah. The amount of sadaqah is specified elsewhere (half a sa' for each circuit of tawaf, etc.). The passage also notes that shaving only the mustache or part of the beard is treated like shaving less than a quarter of the head. The footnotes reference the sources (al-Hidayah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) and clarify a subtle point about the two dams dispute from the previous lesson, but that is tangential. This lesson is meant for memorization: the precise thresholds (less than a limb, less than a day, less than a quarter of the head, fewer than five nails) trigger sadaqah, not dam.

Key Terms
صدقة (sadaqah): A charity payment required for minor violations during ihram, typically half a sa' of wheat or equivalent.
ربع الرأس (rub' al-ra's): One quarter of the head; the threshold for shaving that triggers a dam. Shaving less than a quarter requires sadaqah.
تفث (tafath): The untidy state of a muhrim after leaving ihram (not combing hair, etc.); indulging in full comfort that removes this state requires a dam.

Minor Hajj Violations: Sadaqah and the Excuse Exception
Lists violations requiring sadaqah and the exception for those with excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the minor Hajj violations that require sadaqah and apply the exception for those with a valid excuse.

Core Idea
Minor Hajj violations require only a small charity (sadaqah), not a full blood sacrifice — unless there is a valid excuse, which grants a choice of three compensations.

This lesson examines the category of minor violations (jinaayat) during Hajj that do not warrant a blood sacrifice (dam) but only a charity (sadaqah). The commentator lists specific actions and provides the underlying principle. He then introduces the exception for a muhrim who acts out of necessity, based on the clear Quranic verse and the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah.

Guided Path
1
List the minor violations
Identify the specific actions that incur sadaqah: perfuming less than a limb, covering the head, wearing stitched clothing less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, cutting fewer than five nails, performing tawaf with hadath, omitting some circuits or jamarat, and shaving another's head.
Each of these is considered a minor infraction.
2
Understand the principle
The text states: if an action involves abandoning a wajib or committing a complete benefit contrary to tafath, it requires a dam; otherwise, sadaqah suffices. Apply this principle to the listed violations.
This is the key criterion for categorizing violations.
3
Examine the excuse exception
When a person has a valid excuse (illness, lice, etc.) and performs a normally minor violation (like shaving or perfuming), the ruling changes to a choice among dam, feeding six, or fasting three days. Identify the three options.
The exception is derived from Quran 2:196 and the hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah.
4
Trace the proof
Recite Quran 2:196 and understand its context. The hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah provides the concrete application: the Prophet gave him the choice when he had lice.
The proof is dalil naqli with clear wajh al-dalalah.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether it falls under minor violation (sadaqah) or the excuse exception (choice). Use the principle and the list as reference.
Practice ensures correct application.

And if he perfumed less than a limb, or covered his head, or wore stitched clothing less than a day, or shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut less than five nails... (And if he perfumed less than a limb, or covered his head, or wore stitched clothing less than a day, or shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut less than five nails, mentioned by the author of al-Hidayah and those who followed him, but the correct view is that by delaying and advancing, one blood (sacrifice) becomes obligatory according to him, and the other is for the Quran, so not both are blood for a violation, but one is, and the other is a blood of gratitude. According to them: since no blood becomes obligatory by advancing one ritual over another or delaying it, one blood remains, which is the blood of the Quran. Thus verified by the author of al-Bahr and his student in Manh al-Ghaffar... [1] His saying: 'And if he perfumed' – this along with what is conjoined to it is a condition, and its answer is his following statement: 'He gives in charity half a sa'... etc. This is the beginning of mentioning violations in which blood is not obligatory but charity. The benefits of the mentioned restrictions in previous issues also appear here. The principle in this chapter: whatever involves abandoning an obligatory act of Hajj or committing a complete benefit contrary to the removal of dishevelment requires blood, and what is not like that has charity. [2] His saying: 'less than a quarter of his head' – similarly if he shaved only his mustache or less than a quarter of his beard or part of his neck. (3) His saying: 'or cut' – he said in al-Lubab: 'Every charity obligated in tawaf is for each circuit half a sa', or in throwing pebbles, for each pebble a charity, or in trimming nails, for each nail a charity, or in hunting and plants of the sanctuary, according to the value...' Or cut less than five nails, or five scattered, or performed the arrival tawaf or the farewell tawaf in a state of hadath, or left three of seven (circuits) of the farewell tawaf, or one of the three jamarat: those which are near the mosque of al-Khayf, or what is near it, or al-Aqabah on the day after the Day of Sacrifice, (or shaved the head of another, he gives in charity half a sa' of wheat. And if he perfumed or shaved with an excuse): i.e., perfumed a limb, or shaved a quarter of his head, (he slaughters, or gives in charity three sa's of food to six poor people, or fasts three days). [1] His saying: 'on the day after the Day of Sacrifice' – he restricted it because the Day of Sacrifice has only one throwing. [2] His saying: 'or shaved' – i.e., the muhrim shaved the head of another, whether that other is a halal or a muhrim, and similarly if he shaved his neck or cut his nails. (3) His saying: 'with an excuse' – such as abundance of lice on the head, fever, headache, wound, sores, and other things. (4) His saying: 'or fasted three days' – its basis is His saying: 'And do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place of sacrifice. And whoever among you is ill or has an ailment of his head, then a compensation of fasting or charity or sacrifice.' And this was revealed concerning Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah – may Allah be pleased with him – for lice abounded on his head and he suffered from that during ihram in the year of al-Hudaybiyyah. The Prophet ordered him to shave and gave him the choice between slaughtering a sheep, feeding six poor people (each with half a sa'), or fasting three days. Reported by the authors of the six authentic collections and others.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of al-Wiqayah discusses the category of minor violations (jinaayat) during Hajj that do not require a full blood sacrifice (dam) but only a charity (sadaqah). The commentator begins by listing actions that incur sadaqah: perfuming less than a full limb, covering the head, wearing stitched clothing for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, or cutting fewer than five nails. The principle stated is that any violation involving the abandonment of a wajib or the commission of a complete benefit contrary to the removal of dishevelment (tafath) requires a dam; otherwise, sadaqah suffices. The text then adds more violations: cutting fewer than five fingernails (or five scattered nails), performing the arrival or farewell tawaf in a state of minor impurity (hadath), leaving three of the seven circuits of the farewell tawaf, or omitting one of the three jamarat (the three pillars) on the day after the Day of Sacrifice. For shaving the head of another person, sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat is required. However, if a muhrim perfumes or shaves his own head due to a valid excuse (such as illness or lice), the ruling changes: he has a choice among three options: slaughter a sheep, feed six poor people (three sa's of food), or fast three days. This exception is based directly on the Quranic verse (2:196) and the authentic hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah, who was suffering from lice and was given this choice by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary also clarifies the definition of 'excuse' (udhr) as including lice, fever, headache, wounds, and similar conditions, and even ignorance or forgetfulness according to some authorities.

Key Terms
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity given as compensation for a minor Hajj violation; here, half a sa' of wheat.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep) required as compensation for certain Hajj violations.
بعذر (bi'udhr): With a valid excuse such as illness, lice, or any condition causing harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the principle that determines whether a Hajj violation requires a dam or sadaqah?
A) If the action involves abandoning a wajib or committing a complete benefit contrary to tafath, it requires dam; otherwise, sadaqah.
B) All violations require a dam.
C) All violations require sadaqah.
D) The determination depends on the intention of the pilgrim.

Key Takeaway
Minor violations during Hajj are compensated with sadaqah, but those with a valid excuse have the option of dam, feeding six, or fasting three days.

Expiations for Hajj Violations: Shaving, Perfume, and More
Lists multiple violations and their required expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct expiation for common hajj violations (shaving, perfume, tawaf with impurity) and explain the proof for the three-option fidyah.

Core Idea
Hajj violations require specific expiations: charity, fasting, or sacrifice, depending on the act and excuse.

This passage from the Hanafi manual lists several prohibited acts during Hajj and their required expiations. The key is to distinguish between violations that require a fixed charity (like shaving another's head) and those that allow a choice (like shaving due to an excuse). Understanding the proof from the Quran and the hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah is essential to grasp why the expiation structure is as it is.

Guided Path
1
Classify the violations
Read the list of violations: cutting fewer than five nails, performing tawaf in a state of minor impurity, leaving three circuits of the farewell tawaf, missing one of the three stonings, shaving another's head, applying perfume, and shaving due to an excuse. Group them into those that involve an 'excuse' and those that are intentional without excuse.
The excuse is only mentioned for shaving and perfume.
2
Identify the expiation for each group
For shaving another's head: charity (half sa' of wheat). For applying perfume or shaving due to an excuse: a choice among three options (slaughtering a sheep, feeding six poor persons with three sa's of food, or fasting three days). For other violations (tawaf with impurity, leaving circuits/stones): each requires a specific expiation (not detailed here but implied to be similar to charity or sacrifice).
The passage focuses on the fidyah for excuse-based violations.
3
Examine the proof for the fidyah
The Quranic verse (2:196) states that whoever is ill or has an ailment of the head must offer a ransom of fasting, charity, or sacrifice. The hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah specifies the amounts: slaughtering a sheep, feeding six poor persons (each with half a sa' = 3 sa' total), or fasting three days. The imperative 'فَفِدْيَةٌ' indicates obligation.
Hanafi usul: the amr (command) indicates wujub (obligation).
4
Note the conditions for the fidyah
The fidyah applies only when there is a valid excuse (e.g., lice, fever, headache, wounds). The commentary clarifies that 'excuse' includes illness or harm. If the violation is intentional without excuse, the expiation is different (usually a full animal sacrifice).
Intentional violations require a larger compensation.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Consider a pilgrim who applies perfume because he has a skin condition that requires medicated oil. The ruling: he has the same fidyah options as shaving due to excuse. A pilgrim who cuts his nails intentionally without excuse must give charity (half sa' per nail? not specified, but a general principle).
Use qiyas to extend the ruling to similar cases of excuse.

[1] His saying: 'on the day after the Day of Sacrifice' – he restricted it because on the Day of Sacrifice there is only one stoning. [2] His saying: 'or shaved' – i.e., the muhrim shaved the head of another, whether that other is halal or muhrim, and similarly if he shaved his neck or cut his nails. (3) His saying: 'due to an excuse' – such as many lice on the head, fever, headache, wound, sores, and other things. (4) His saying: 'or fasts three days' – the basis for it is His statement: 'And do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place of sacrifice. And whoever among you is ill or has an ailment of the head, then a ransom of fasting or charity or sacrifice.' And this was revealed concerning Ka'b bin 'Ujrah, may Allah be pleased with him, for many lice appeared on his head, and he suffered from that while in ihram in the year of Hudaybiyyah, so the Prophet commanded him to shave, and gave him the choice between slaughtering a sheep, or feeding six poor persons – for each poor person half a sa' – or fasting three days. Source pages p. 621

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on violations during Hajj (jinaayat al-hajj) and their required expiations. The matn lists various prohibited acts: cutting fewer than five nails, performing tawaf in a state of minor impurity (hadath), omitting three circuits of the farewell tawaf, missing one of the three stonings, shaving another's head, applying perfume, or shaving due to an excuse. For each, the expiation is specified: if one shaves another's head, he gives half a sa' of wheat in charity; if one applies perfume or shaves due to an excuse, he has the choice of slaughtering a sheep, giving three sa's of food to six poor persons, or fasting three days. The commentary by the author expands on these rulings, clarifying that 'on the day after the Day of Sacrifice' excludes the Day of Sacrifice itself, which has only one stoning. It also explains that shaving another's head is restricted to the muhrim shaving a halal or muhrim person, and similarly for cutting nails. The 'excuse' includes lice, fever, headache, wounds, etc. The proof for the expiation of shaving due to excuse is the Quranic verse (2:196) and the hadith of Ka'b bin 'Ujrah, where the Prophet gave him the option of sacrifice, charity, or fasting. This demonstrates the principle that necessary violations (due to illness or harm) are expiable by a choice among three acts, whereas intentional violations without excuse require the full penalty (blood or charity). The passage underscores the structured nature of Hajj expiations, where the severity of the violation and presence of an excuse determine the type of kaffarah.

Key Terms
جناية (jināyah): A violation or transgression committed during the state of ihram in Hajj or Umrah.
فدية (fidyah): An expiation or ransom for violating the prohibition of shaving the head due to illness or harm, consisting of slaughtering a sheep, feeding six poor persons, or fasting three days.
صاع (ṣā'): A unit of volume measurement used for food charity; approximately 3.036 kg in weight for wheat, but here half a sa' (for shaving another's head) and three sa's (for the fidyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Fast three days
D) Perform an additional tawaf

Key Takeaway
The fidyah for shaving due to excuse offers three options; other violations have fixed expiations such as half a sa' of wheat for shaving another's head.

Sexual Intercourse Invalidates Hajj
Explains the ruling on sexual intercourse before standing at Arafah and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse before wuquf and apply the conditions for completion and repetition.

Core Idea
Intercourse before wuquf invalidates Hajj but requires completion, sacrifice, and repetition; spouses remain together.

This lesson examines the most severe violation during Hajj—sexual intercourse before the obligatory standing at Arafah. The Hanafi school rules that while the Hajj becomes fasid, the pilgrim must complete the rituals and perform a replacement Hajj the following year. The proof comes from the prophetic command to the man from Judham.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act and its effect on Hajj
The passage states that sexual intercourse (wat') before the obligatory standing (wuquf farḍ) invalidates the Hajj (yufsid). Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the invalidation entails.
The invalidation is fasād, not batil; the pilgrim must still complete the current Hajj.
2
Analyze the three required actions after invalidation
The text says 'yumdi wa yadhbah wa yaqdi' – he must proceed, slaughter a sheep, and repeat the Hajj the following year. Understand each term and its implication.
'Yaqdi' is metaphorical; it is actually repetition (i'ada) because the time for Hajj is a lifetime.
3
Examine the rule regarding the spouses
The phrase 'wa lam yaftariqa' means the spouses are not to separate; they continue together and must travel for the qada Hajj together.
This is a distinctive Hanafi point; some schools may require separation.
4
Locate the prophetic proof (dalil)
The passage cites the hadith of the man from Judham who had intercourse while in ihram. The Prophet commanded: 'Complete your rites and offer a sacrificial animal.' This hadith is the basis.
The hadith is mursal but considered reliable by al-Arna'ut.
5
Distinguish between excuses and intentional violations
The passage extends the ruling to all prohibited acts of ihram if committed with an excuse (error, forgetfulness, etc.). But if intentional without excuse, only blood or charity is obligatory.
This affects the type of expiation: for intentional, no option of food or fasting.

And attached to this is the commission of every prohibited act of ihram if it is with an excuse. As for error, forgetfulness, unconsciousness, coercion, sleep, and inability to perform the expiation, these are not excuses with regard to the choice. And if he commits the prohibited act intentionally without excuse, then what is obligatory is blood or charity, not food or fasting. Thus in al-Lubab. [1] His saying: 'standing' – with tanwin, so what follows it is an adjective, or without tanwin so what follows it is annexed to it and the annexation is explanatory; i.e., before a standing that is obligatory, which is the standing at Arafah; and it excludes the standing at Muzdalifah, as will be mentioned later. [2] His saying: 'he must proceed' – i.e., it is obligatory upon him to complete that Hajj, and to offer a sacrificial animal, and to perform his Hajj again in the coming year; thus the Messenger of Allah said, reported by al-Bayhaqi and Abu Dawud in al-Marasil. [3] His saying: 'he performs again' – its being termed a 'qada' is metaphorical for the obligatory, for it is a repetition, not a qada, because its time is a lifetime; and in the absolute wording is an indication that he also performs the supererogatory (Hajj) again, due to its being binding by commencement. Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage addresses the most severe violation during Hajj: sexual intercourse (wat') before the wuquf at Arafah. The ruling is that it invalidates (yufsid) the Hajj. However, the pilgrim must complete the current Hajj (yumdi) and then slaughter a sheep (yadhbah). Additionally, he must perform a replacement Hajj (yaqdi) the following year. Importantly, the spouses are not to be separated (lam yaftariqa) during the entire process; they remain married and travel together for the qada Hajj. The commentary clarifies that 'obligatory standing' refers specifically to the standing at Arafah, not Muzdalifah. The term 'qada' is a metaphorical usage here, as the time for performing Hajj is one's entire lifetime, so it is actually a repetition (i'ada) rather than a make-up (qada) in the technical sense. The passage then expands to the general rule: all prohibited acts of ihram, when committed with an excuse, are treated similarly to the fidyah for shaving (i.e., option of blood, charity, or fasting). But if committed intentionally without excuse, only blood or charity is obligatory—not food or fasting. This distinction highlights the Hanafi position that intention and excuse affect the type of expiation. The proof is the hadith of the man from Judham who had intercourse with his wife while both were in ihram, and the Prophet commanded them to complete their rites and offer a sacrificial animal. This hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi as a mursal (but the chain is considered trustworthy by al-Arna'ut). The passage underscores the gravity of sexual intercourse during Hajj and the structured penalties.

Key Terms
وقف فرض (wuqūf farḍ): The obligatory standing at 'Arafah during Hajj; the crucial ritual upon which the entire Hajj depends.
فساد (fasād): Invalidation of the Hajj due to a major violation (like intercourse before wuquf), requiring completion and repetition.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Here used metaphorically to mean 'repetition' of the Hajj in the following year, not technically qada (which applies to missed obligations).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sexual intercourse before wuquf invalidates Hajj but requires completion, sacrifice, and repetition; spouses remain together.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Sexual Intercourse Before Wuquf: Ruling and Hanafi Position
Ruling on sexual intercourse before wuquf with proof and dispute on separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse before wuquf and explain why the spouses are not required to separate during the makeup Hajj.

Core Idea
Intercourse before wuquf corrupts the Hajj, but the spouses need not separate—only sacrifice and repeat.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the severe ruling on sexual intercourse during Hajj before the obligatory standing at Arafah. Even if forgetful, the Hajj is corrupted, requiring completion, sacrifice, and a make-up Hajj. The Hanafi position also holds that the spouses are not forced to separate during the make-up journey, contrary to other schools. Understanding this ruling clarifies the gravity of violating ihram and the school's approach to expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sexual intercourse while in ihram before the wuquf at Arafah. The ruling: it corrupts (yufsid) the Hajj.
Even if forgetful (nāsiyān), the ruling applies.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a hadith of the Prophet (ṣ) commanding completion, sacrifice, and make-up, reported by al-Bayhaqi and Abu Dawud.
The hadith is considered a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence).
3
Identify the consequences
Three consequences: (1) complete the corrupted Hajj, (2) slaughter a sacrificial animal (badanah or sheep), (3) perform a make-up Hajj the following year.
This is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on separation
Malik and Zufar require spouses to separate from ihram; Shafiʿi (old opinion) requires separation at the place of offense. The Hanafi school holds that separation is not obligatory, only recommended.
The Hanafi view is based on interpreting reports from ʿAlī and ʿUmar as precaution, not obligation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that the spouses are not required to separate. This is the relied-upon view in the school, as stated in al-Hidayah and other texts.
The opposing views are respected but considered marjuh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١] قوله : وقوف ; بالتنوين فما بعده وصف، أو بغيره فما بعده مضاف إليه والإضافة بيانية؛ أي قبل وقوف هو فرض، وهو الوقوف بعرفة، واحترز عن وقوف المزدلفة، كما سيأتي ذكره. [٢] قوله : ويمضي؛ أي يجب عليه أن يتم ذلك الحج، ويهدي هدياً، ويقضي حجه في العام القابل، هكذا قاله رسول الله ﷺ، أخرجه البيهقي وأبو داود في «المراسيل». [٣] قوله: ويقضي؛ تسميته قضاء مجاز في الفرض، فإنّه إعادة لا قضاء؛ لأنّ وقته العمر، وفي الإطلاق إشارة إلى قضائه النفل أيضاً للزومه بالشروع. [٤] قوله: ولم يفترقا؛ أي لا يلزم على الزوجين أن لا يصاحبا، بل يفترقا في سفر قضاء ذلك الحج الذي أفسداه. (أي ليس عليه أن يفارقها في قضاء ما أفسداه، وعند مالك [يفارقها] إذا خرجا من بيتهما، وعند زفر [يفارقها] إذا أحرما، وعند الشافعي [يفارقها] إذا بلغا المكان الذي واقعها فيه. [١] قوله: وعند مالك... الخ؛ السر في الافتراق زجرهما، ولئلا يتذكر ما سبق منهما فيقعا فيه، وقد نقل عن علي ﷲ أنه أمر بالافتراق من عند الإحرام، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ» واختاره، وذهب إليه زفر أيضاً. وعن عمر أنه أمر به حين وصولهما إلى المكان الذي ارتكبا فيه الجناية، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وهو الذي اختاره الشافعي، وهذا كله عندنا محمول على الاحتياط والأولوية لا على الوجوب. [٢] قوله: إذا خرجا؛ هكذا ذكر في «الهداية» وغيره، والمذكور في أكثر كتب المالكية: هو الافتراق عند الإحرام. [٣] قوله: عند الشافعي له؛ أي في قوله القديم، وأما في قوله الجديد، فهو موافق لنا.)
And his sexual intercourse, even if forgetfully, before the obligatory standing (at Arafah) corrupts his Hajj, and he must proceed (complete it) and slaughter, and make it up next year, and they do not separate. And attached to it is the commission of any prohibition from the prohibitions of ihram if it is with an excuse. As for error, forgetfulness, unconsciousness, coercion, sleep, and inability to perform the expiation, these are not excuses with regard to choice. And if one commits a prohibition intentionally without an excuse, then the obligatory (expiation) is blood or charity, not food or fasting. Thus in 'al-Lubab'. [1] His saying: 'standing' with tanwin then what follows is an adjective, or without it then what follows is a genitive construct and the idafah is explanatory; i.e., before a standing that is obligatory, which is the standing at Arafah, and it excludes the standing at Muzdalifah, as will be mentioned. [2] His saying: 'and he must proceed' i.e., it is obligatory for him to complete that Hajj, and sacrifice a sacrificial animal, and make up his Hajj the following year; thus said the Messenger of Allah, reported by al-Bayhaqi and Abu Dawud in 'al-Maraseel'. [3] His saying: 'and make up' the naming of it as 'qada'' is metaphorical in the obligatory, for it is a repetition not a make-up because its time is the whole of life, and in the absolute expression there is an indication that he also makes up the supererogatory (Hajj) due to its being obligated by commencement. [4] His saying: 'and they do not separate' i.e., it is not necessary for the spouses not to accompany each other, but they separate in the journey of making up that Hajj which they corrupted. (That is, he is not required to separate from her in making up what they corrupted. According to Malik, he separates from her when they leave their house; according to Zufar, he separates when they assume ihram; according to al-Shafi'i, he separates when they reach the place where he had intercourse with her. [1] His saying: 'According to Malik...' the secret in separation is to deter them, lest they remember what happened between them and fall into it again. It has been narrated from 'Ali that he ordered separation from the time of ihram, reported by Malik in 'al-Muwatta' and he chose it, and Zufar also adopted it. And from 'Umar that he ordered it when they reached the place where they committed the offense, reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, and this is what al-Shafi'i chose. All of this according to us is interpreted as precaution and preference, not as obligation. [2] His saying: 'when they leave' thus it is mentioned in 'al-Hidayah' and others, but what is mentioned in most Maliki books is that the separation is at the time of ihram. [3] His saying: 'according to al-Shafi'i' i.e., in his old opinion; as for his new opinion, he agrees with us.)
Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah on sexual intercourse during Hajj before the obligatory standing at Arafah. The matn states that such intercourse corrupts the Hajj, even if done forgetfully, and the pilgrim must complete the corrupted Hajj, sacrifice an animal, and perform a makeup Hajj the following year. The spouses are not required to separate, meaning they may travel together for the makeup Hajj. The commentary clarifies that the ‘standing’ refers to the standing at Arafah, not Muzdalifah. The ruling is extended to all prohibitions of ihram if committed with an excuse, but error, forgetfulness, etc. are not excuses regarding the choice of expiation; if done intentionally without excuse, the obligation is blood (sacrifice) or charity, not food or fasting. The passage then presents a dispute on whether the spouses must separate during the makeup journey. The Hanafi position is that separation is not obligatory; it is only precautionary. Malik and Zufar require separation from the start of ihram, while Shafi‘i requires it at the location of the offense. The commentary notes that these views are based on reports from ‘Ali and ‘Umar but are not obligatory according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
وقوف (wuquf): The standing at Arafah on the ninth of Dhul-Hijjah, which is the essential pillar of Hajj.
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial camel or cow, required for major violations like intercourse before wuquf.
يفترقا (yaftariqa): The spouses separating during the makeup Hajj; the Hanafi view is that it is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse before wuquf during Hajj?
A) It invalidates the Hajj, but no expiation is required.
B) It invalidates the Hajj; the pilgrim must complete it, sacrifice an animal, and perform a makeup Hajj the next year.
C) It does not invalidate the Hajj if done forgetfully.
D) The spouses must separate during the makeup Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Intercourse before wuquf corrupts the Hajj, requiring completion, sacrifice, and make-up; spouses are not required to separate.

Sexual Intercourse After Wuquf and During Umrah: Rulings and Disputes
Rulings on intercourse after wuquf, halq, and during Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sexual intercourse after wuquf, after halq, and during Umrah, and explain the Hanafi position on spouse separation compared to Malik and Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Intercourse after wuquf requires a camel; after halq, a sheep; in Umrah, four circuits determine invalidation.

This lesson examines the legal impact of sexual intercourse at various stages of Hajj and Umrah. The matn provides clear rulings on required sacrifices and whether the pilgrimage is invalidated. It also addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: must spouses separate during the makeup Hajj? Understanding these distinctions is essential for both ritual validity and practical guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (sexual intercourse) and at what stage (after wuquf, after halq, during Umrah before/after 4 circuits). Note the hukm level: does it invalidate? What sacrifice is wajib?
After wuquf = no invalidation + badanah; after halq = no invalidation + shah; Umrah before 4 circuits = invalidation + qada.
2
Locate the threshold for Umrah
Identify why four circuits of tawaf are the dividing line. The commentary explains: before four, the majority of tawaf is not done, so the offense is graver; after four, the majority is done, so only a sacrifice is due.
This is a key Hanafi principle: completion of the majority (akthar) lightens the penalty.
3
Note the sacrifice required
Distinguish between badanah (camel/cow) for serious violations (after wuquf) and shah (sheep) for lighter ones (after halq, after 4 circuits in Umrah).
Badanah is wajib for major infractions; shah suffices for minor ones.
4
Examine the dispute on spouse separation
Understand the issue: when Hajj is corrupted by intercourse, must the spouses separate during the makeup journey? The Hanafi position is that separation is not obligatory, only recommended. Malik and Shafi'i (old view) require separation.
The Hanafi school interprets the reports from 'Ali and 'Umar as precautionary, not legally binding.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
See how the Hanafi school weighs the evidence: the Prophet did not order separation, so silence is given weight over the companion reports. Therefore, separation is not wajib.
This tarjih is affirmed by al-Marghinani and later Hanafi authorities.

[١] قوله: وعند مالك... الخ؛ السر في الافتراق زجرهما، ولئلا يتذكر ما سبق منهما فيقعا فيه، وقد نقل عن علي . أنه أمر بالافتراق من عند الإحرام، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ» واختاره، وذهب إليه زفر أيضاً. وعن عمر أنه أمر به حين وصولهما إلى المكان الذي ارتكبا فيه الجناية»، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وهو الذي اختاره الشافعي، وهذا كله عندنا محمول على الاحتياط والأولوية لا على الوجوب. [٢] قوله: إذا خرجا؛ هكذا ذكر في «الهداية» وغيره، والمذكور في أكثر كتب المالكية: هو الافتراق عند الإحرام. [٣] قوله: عند الشافعي له؛ أي في قوله القديم، وأما في قوله الجديد، فهو موافق لنا. (٤) قوله: وبعد وقوفه... الخ؛ يعني لو جامع بعد الفراغ من وقوف عرفة، وهو الركن الأعظم لم يفسد حجّه، بل يجب عليه ذبح إبل أو بقر والقضاء، وإن جامع بعد الحلق قبل الطواف يجب ذبح شاة لخفة الجناية. (٥) قوله: مفسد للعمرة؛ لأنه لما لم يطف أربعة أشواط لم يوجد الأكثر، بخلاف ما إذا طاف الأربعة، فإنّه وجد حينئذ الأكثر، فخفت الجناية.
(And after his standing it does not corrupt, and a camel (badanah) is obligatory, and after shaving (halq) a sheep. And in his Umrah, before his tawaf of four circuits, it corrupts it, so he must proceed, slaughter, and make up; after four (circuits) he slaughters and it does not corrupt): i.e., his intercourse in his Umrah before he performs four circuits of tawaf corrupts the Umrah, so it is obligatory to proceed with it, slaughter, and make up; after four circuits, slaughter is obligatory by it and the Umrah is not corrupted by it. [1] His saying: 'According to Malik...' the secret in separation is to deter them, lest they remember what happened between them and fall into it again. It has been narrated from 'Ali that he ordered separation from the time of ihram, reported by Malik in 'al-Muwatta' and he chose it, and Zufar also adopted it. And from 'Umar that he ordered it when they reached the place where they committed the offense, reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, and this is what al-Shafi'i chose. All of this according to us is interpreted as precaution and preference, not as obligation. [2] His saying: 'when they leave' thus it is mentioned in 'al-Hidayah' and others, but what is mentioned in most Maliki books is that the separation is at the time of ihram. [3] His saying: 'according to al-Shafi'i' i.e., in his old opinion; as for his new opinion, he agrees with us. (4) His saying: 'And after his standing...' means: if he has intercourse after completing the standing of Arafah, which is the greatest pillar, it does not corrupt his Hajj, but he must slaughter camels or cows and make up; if he has intercourse after shaving but before tawaf, he must slaughter a sheep due to the lightness of the offense. (5) His saying: 'corrupts the Umrah' because when he has not performed four circuits, the majority (of the tawaf) has not been done, unlike when he has performed four circuits, then the majority has been done, so the offense is lighter.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from the matn on sexual intercourse during Hajj after the standing at Arafah, after shaving (halq), and during Umrah, followed by a inter-madhhab dispute on the separation of spouses. The matn states: after wuquf, intercourse does not invalidate the Hajj but requires a camel (badanah); after halq but before tawaf, a sheep suffices. In Umrah, if intercourse occurs before completing four circuits of tawaf, the Umrah is invalidated and must be completed, a sacrifice made, and the Umrah made up; if after four circuits, only a sacrifice is due and the Umrah remains valid. The commentary explains the logic: before four circuits, the majority of tawaf is not yet done, so the transgression is graver. Then the passage repeats the dispute about spouses separating during the makeup journey, this time in more detail: the Hanafi view is that separation is not obligatory but only precautionary. Reports from 'Ali (separation from ihram) and 'Umar (separation at the location) are cited, and the Hanafi school interprets these as recommended, not required. The commentary also notes that Shafi'i's new opinion agrees with the Hanafi view on the separation issue.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow sacrificed for serious violations; required after intercourse after wuquf.
شاة (shah): A sheep (goat) sacrificed for lighter violations, e.g., intercourse after halq before tawaf.
أربعة أشواط (arba'atu ashwat): Four circuits of tawaf; the threshold for determining invalidation of Umrah by intercourse.
قضاء (qada): Makeup; required when Umrah is invalidated by intercourse before four circuits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the required sacrifice if a pilgrim has intercourse after standing at Arafah (wuquf) during Hajj?
A) A sheep (shah)
B) A camel or cow (badanah)
C) Nothing, as the Hajj is invalidated
D) A sacrifice is not required if the couple separates immediately

Key Takeaway
After wuquf, intercourse does not invalidate Hajj but requires a badanah; after halq, a shah suffices; in Umrah, the four-circuit threshold determines invalidation; and Hanafis do not obligate spouse separation during the makeup journey.
